Annual Report 2016
(D.O. Letter from Mr. Naveed Akram Cheema,  Chairman, Federal Public Service Commission(FPSC) to Mr. Mamnoon Hussain President, Islamic Republic of Pakistan)
(Annual Report 2016)
Naveed Akram Cheema
Chairman,
Tel-------------------------
No-----------Islamabad,  date----------------
Mr. President,
I have the privilege to present the Annual Report of the Federal Public Service Commission (FPSC) for the year 2016, in accordance with Section  9 of the FPSC Ordinance 1977 which, inter alia, provides that a copy of this report is to be laid before the National Assembly and the Senate. 
The report covers functions, activities, observations and recommendations of the Commission from 1st January to 31st December, 2016. 
I. Statutory Functions of FPSC
2.  Under the guiding principles of Articles 18, 25, 27, 34, 36, and 38 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan 1973 and under Section  7 of the Federal Public Service Commission Ordinance 1977, the Commission performs its statutory functions, wherein it ensures: 
a. Conducting tests and examinations for recruitment of persons to All-Pakistan Services, the civil services of the federation and civil posts in connection with affairs of the federation in basic scales 1 6and above or equivalent;
b. Tendering advice to the President of Pakistan on methods and principles to be followed in making initial appointments, appointments by promotion to posts in BS 1 8and above and transfer from one service or occupational group to another;
c. Holding examinations for promotion and;
d. Performing quasi-judicial functions by taking decisions on representations and review petitions of aggrieved candidates.
3. On 17th February 2016, the Prime Minister of Pakistan constituted a committee under the headship of Mr. Zahid Hamid, the then Minister for Climate Change to deliberate on the ways and means to make the Federal Public Service Commission a vibrant body and to examine the possibility of its conversion from a statutory to a constitutional body.
Deliberations of the committee with key stakeholders are underway. 
The Commission takes a leadership role in strengthening and revamping the recruitment system to build a competent human resource base for the civil services of Pakistan. 
While continuing; to deliver its core services, the Commission has made significant progress in enhancing and fulfilling its goals and targets set forth for the year 2016. 
The Commission takes pride in the gigantic task of skillfully handling and processing 20,71 7CSS and 8,75,281 applications to the posts of BS 16 and above during the year under review. 
This report presents a detailed review of the Commission's performance, accomplishments and areas of concern during 2016, as given below: 
II. Performance Highlights
4. Globalization and technological revolution has thrown severe challenges to the traditional recruitment system during the last two decades. 
With more erudite citizenry, extremely vigilant and liberal electronic media, intense accountability of public policy makers through a vibrant judiciary, civil servants are finding themselves under ever keener scrutiny. Ubiquitous use of internet and social media has raised the level of expectations in terms of speed. 
quality and personalization of public service delivery which is the hallmark of good governance. 
This requires adoption of an efficient, transparent and merit-based system of recruitment for the civil services of Pakistan enabling the state to deliver desired public services to the citizens in a most effective and efficient manner. 
While effectively addressing growing challenges, the Federal Public Service Commission maintained trust of the public through its policies of transparency, fairness. impartiality and professionalism during the year under report. 
The statistics on the number of applications, conduct of tests/examinations, interviews and the nominations made during the year show a continued high level of employee engagement across FPSC. An overview of the core functions accomplished by the FPSC is as follows: 
i) Examinations and Tests Conducted during 2016: 
The Commission carried out and finalized the allocation of candidates to various Occupational Groups and Services on the basis of Central Superior Services (CSS) Competitive Examination(CE) 2015 and conducted the CSS CE 2016, Final Passing Out Examination (FPOE) of twelve Occupational Groups and Services which determines the final merit and inter-se seniority and Professional Screening Tests/interviews for selection against posts in BS-16 and above requisitioned by Ministries/Divisions/Departments by General Recruitment. 
Summary of the same is as follows: 
a) Central Superior Services Competitive Examination 201 5and 2016: The Commission announced final merit of CE-201 5on 24.04.2016.
Highlights of CE 2015 & 2016are as below: 
CSS CE 2015
CSS CE 2016
Total Number of Applicants
Total Candidates APpeared
Qualified in written
Finally Qualified
Vacancies Available
Candidates Allocated
Male
Female
Vacancies Carried Forward
The scheme of syllabi (1981) for competitive examination was reviewed by the Commission in 2015 in collaboration with the Higher Education Commission and country-wide Universities' professors/subject specialists. 
The Commission conducted the CSS CE 2016 based on the new syllabi which was one of the important milestones achieved during 2016. 
Under the new scheme marks of many subjects were rationalized and six new optional subjects viz Governance and Public Policy, Criminology, Gender Studies, Environmental Sciences, Anthropology and Town Planning & Urban Management were added to the list. 
Besides, Comparative Study of Major Religions was introduced for non-Muslims. 
Optional subjects were also re-grouped to provide level playing field to both students of natural sciences and social sciences. 
According to the CSS CE 2016 result, only 202 candidates qualified inwritten part of the examination. 
A total of 20717 aspirants applied but only 964 3appeared depicting that majority of them was not serious. 
The Examiners also observed a decline in general performance of candidates and shared concerns on declining standard of education.
The Examiners' Assessment Reports identified poor expression, lack of analytical skills and critical approach, inability to comprehend issues as some of the reasons for massive failures. 
To further examine the issue, the Commission constituted a Consultative Group with representation from Members of the Commission. 
Extensive consultations were held with Higher Education Commission, Ministry of Federal Education and Professional Training, Capital Administration & Development Division and Provincial Education Departments to suggest measures for improvement. 
The Consultative Group in its initial findings was critical of the coaching centers/guide books/guess papers used by the candidates. It also underlined the need for improvement in standard of education. 
Members of the Commission also carried out motivational talks at well reputed national universities and kept the academia informed of the performance of the respective educational institutions in national level competitive exam. 
A summary of Examiners' Assessment Reports has also been placed on FPSC website for general information of the public and aspiring candidates.
b) Recruitment for Technical and Professional Ex-Cadre Posts: Reforms have been carried out to bring qualitative improvement in methods of general recruitment for all posts in BS-1 6and above including ex-cadre services. 
The selection process was further improved through revision of syllabi and test schemes. The objective was to make the selection more competitive and to select those candidates who were better equipped with the skills set required to perform the job. Test schemes and syllabi for 27 9recruitment cases were designed in 2016. 
Highlights of General Recruitment 2016
Number of vacancies (BS 1 6and above) processed during 2016
Applications Processed
Cancidates scheduled for interview
Candidates scheduled for personal hearing
Candidates recommended for appointment
Vacancies remained unfilled
Number of vacancies which were under process and carried over to the next year
c) Final Passing Out Exam inations held during 2016: The Commission conducted Final Passing Out Examinations for the Probationers of Occupational Groups and Services after completion of respective specialized training. 
The examination is important as it determines inter seniority in their respective Groups and Services. 
In all, 298 probationers appeared in FPOEs and only 199 qualified the examination. 
The highest pass percentage was in Police Service of Pakistan and highest failure ratios were in Inland Revenue Service and Pakistan Administrative Service.
ii) Appeals of candidates against their rejection: 
Section 7(3) (a) of the FPSC Ordinance provides opportunity of Representation and Review Petition against any decision of the Commission. 
During the period under report, the Commission afforded personal hearing to 123 5candidates and decided their representation on case to case basis. 
The candidates whose representations were accepted, were called for interview and remaining representations were dismissed. 
Under Section 7(3) (b) 52 review petitions against dismissal of representations were filed by the aggrieved candidates which were also examined and decided by the Commission in accordance with rules. 
iii) Advice on Rules for Recruitment: 
The Commission received 118 cases from government entities for approval of recruitment rules under Section  7(1) (b) of the FPSC Ordinance 1977. 
The Commission approved 35 cases, whereas  3cases were considered unfit and 80 cases were processed to remove deficiencies in consultation with the concerned government entities.
iv) Cases where implementation of Advice of the Commission was delayed: 
In  5 cases, offer of appointment was delayed by the concerned Ministry/ Division/ Department.
v) Cases where Advice of the Commission was not observed: It is mandatory for all Ministries/Divisions/Departments to solicit consent of the Commission for extension in contract appointment beyond  2 years against all civil positions. 
During the period under report,  6cases of extension in contract appointments were received in the Commission. 
In 4 cases, extension for a period of  6months was granted subject to requisitioning the respective vacancies for regular filling in terms of Rule 10 & 1 4of the Civil Servants (Appointment, Promotion and Transfer) Rules 1973, but requisitions for the said posts were not furnished to the FPSC. 
III. Key Initiatives
A number of initiatives to cater for increased workload of the Commission were taken in the recent past. 
Pakistan's system of government
(Federal, Provincial and District)
(In light of Constitution of Pakistan and Federal/Provincial Rules)

foreword
Paving the way for the implementation of the national language Urdu in the official, office and judicial spheres of national life is one of the main aims and objectives of the National Language Promotion Institute.
To achieve this goal, the organization has been active since its inception and has been achieving its goals by publishing several books related to office language.
What is the system of government in Pakistan? And at what level what style is prevalent? On this subject, Mr. Jamshed Alam wrote articles which were published in the journal "Ilm wa Fan" for the promotion of national language.
In these articles, the organizational structure of the government at the federal, provincial and district levels, the system of government of the provinces, the relations and procedures between the federation and the provinces were described in detail.
These articles were of importance so it was decided to convert these articles into a book.
When Mr. Jamshed Alam was requested to revise these articles, he repeated the process of amendments, additions and deletions, re-drafting it according to the latest information and including Gilgit-Baltistan.
Mr. Jamshed Alam has a long experience in government service and is intimately familiar with the basic and additional requirements of adapting the office system to the national language.
He fulfilled the lack of material in Urdu on this subject through this book.
His services in making the national language Urdu an official language are commendable.
I am also grateful to Dr. Anjum Hameed and Mr. Shakeel Ahmad Mangaluri for using their skills to bring it into book form.
I am sure that this book will be of interest to civil servants, students of political science and people from other walks of life.
Iftikhar Arif

Chapter 1
Constitutional background
1. Constitution of the State: Basis of Organizational Structure
A constitution is the basic law of a country that defines the ideals, concepts, basic principles of its internal management and the boundaries of duties and powers between its various departments.
In ancient times, the most important function of the constitution was to determine who should rule the country.
The criteria for assigning the political authority of a country to an individual reflected the emotional attitudes and behavior of the social system of that country.
Whatever the form of the constitution, it used to influence the morals of the people.
Although modern constitutions are more complex, the laws and regulations governing the acquisition and exercise of governmental authority in a state generally cover the basic beliefs, ideas, concepts, and values of a society and its social behaviors in daily life. They represent behavior and manners.
There is a majority of Muslims in Pakistan (97 percent) and the distinguishing feature of Muslims is the belief of Tawheed and the code of life based on the teachings of the last Prophet Muhammad.
In an Islamic society built on the basis of the Book and the Sunnah, without discrimination of color, caste and creed, the protection of basic human rights, direct or indirect involvement of every person from an ordinary citizen to the President of the State in the management of the government. And the sense of accountability, the rule of justice and the high values of unity of thought are fostered.
According to democratic principles, the Constitution of Pakistan is the expression of the wishes of the majority living in this country.
Allama Muhammad Iqbal and Quaid-e-Azam Muhammad Ali Jinnah have given a clear indication of these aspirations in their various sermons.
Allama Muhammad Iqbal in his famous sermon at Allahabad (1930) said in order to improve the separate existence of Muslims in the subcontinent and their social, economic and political conditions:
"After a long and deep study of Islamic law, I have come to the conclusion that if this law is well understood and implemented, every person is guaranteed at least the right to livelihood, but the implementation and development of Shariat is a free Muslim. It is not possible in this country without the state.
Quaid-e-Azam explained the concept of Pakistan several times during the Pakistan Movement and after the establishment of Pakistan. You said:
"Muslims demand Pakistan, where they can rule according to their own code of life, their own cultural development, their own traditions and Islamic law."
(Meeting of Sarhad Muslim League, held in Peshawar on November 21, 1945)
"Every Muslim knows that the Quranic teachings are not limited to worship and ethics, but the Holy Quran is the religion, faith and law of life for Muslims.
That is, it is a collection of religious, social, commercial, cultural, military and penal rules.
Our Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, has ordered us to study it carefully so that it leads to individual and collective guidance of Muslims.
The Quaid-e-Azam while explaining his motto after the establishment of Pakistan said:
"Our aim was to create a state where we can live as free human beings, flourish in the light of our civilization and where the Islamic concept of social justice has a chance to flourish." .
(Address to the officers of the Government of Pakistan, October 1947)
2. The Islamic Basis of the Constitution of Pakistan
(1) Objectives of the Resolution: After the establishment of Pakistan, when the constitution of this independent state was being drawn up, in March 1949, on the motion of Mr. Liaquat Ali Khan, the Prime Minister of Pakistan, the Constituent Assembly passed a resolution on March 12, 1949, which It is known as Resolution of Objectives.
In this resolution, the aims and objectives of the future constitution have been described.
This resolution has been included in the preamble of the Constitution of Pakistan.
It is clearly declared in it.
"That Allah Ta'ala is the absolute ruler of the entire universe without participation, and that the people of Pakistan will use the authority and authority within the limits set by Allah is a sacred trust; It is the intention of the people of Pakistan to establish a system in which the State shall exercise its powers and sovereignty through elected representatives of the people; The principles of democracy, freedom, equality, tolerance and social justice, as interpreted by Islam, will be fully implemented in the state; And Muslims will be enabled in individual and collective spheres of action to correct their lives in accordance with Islamic teachings as determined in the Holy Qur'an and the Sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ.
(2) State religion: According to the above clear declaration, it is written in Article 2 of the Constitution that Islam shall be the state religion of Pakistan.
3. Federal nature of the Constitution of Pakistan
In the preamble of the constitution, it is declared that the territories in this kingdom which are currently included or merged in Pakistan and such other territories which will be included or merged in Pakistan later will form a federation in which the units will have their powers and sovereignty. but with such limitations and restrictions as may be prescribed, shall be sovereign.
Federalism: It is a way of creating a unified structure of a state so that powers can be divided between the central and regional governments in such a way that each government is independent in a certain area.
The territory of a federal state is divided into units (eg states, cantons, provinces, republics).
These units are often of distinctive importance as geo-civilizational or historical units.
Many government agencies are established at both the national and regional (provincial in Pakistan) levels.
Both types of governments effectively control the same territory and population.
Thus the citizens of a federal state belong to two political communities at the same time.
Constitutionally (in Pakistan) with respect to the duties assigned to the provincial level government, there is a specific provincial community with its own common interests for citizens permanently residing in a province; Regarding the duties assigned to the federal government, the entire nation of Pakistan is one community and they have common interests with regard to the entire country.
In a true federal state, both levels of government derive their powers directly from the constitution and one government cannot override the jurisdiction of the other.
In the politics of a federal state, the balance of power between the two levels of government and the balance of loyalty of citizens between their country and territory play an active and dynamic role.
Otherwise, the centralist forces may become strong enough to negate the autonomy of the provincial government, while the pro-devolution forces may work to break up the country itself.
Therefore, for a federal state to survive, it is essential that independent political forces exist to support and back up all levels of government.
4. Fundamental Rights in the Constitution: A Guide to Legislation
Fundamental rights have been given utmost importance in the Constitution of Pakistan.
A law that is inconsistent with fundamental rights can be declared null and void.
The Majlis-e-Shura has been mandated that no law can be made contrary to the fundamental rights except for the exceptions mentioned in the constitution.
These fundamental rights within the ambit of law are as follows:
(1) Personal Security: No person shall be deprived of life or liberty except as permitted by law.
(2)	 Protection from Arrest and Detention: No person who has been arrested shall be detained without being informed as soon as possible of the reasons for the arrest, nor shall he be allowed to consult any legal person of his choice and This will deprive the right to offer cleaning.
The arrested/detained person shall be produced before a Magistrate within 24 hours.
(3)	Prohibition of slavery and forced labour
(4)	Protection from punishment by effective ex post facto law
(5)	Protection against double punishment and self-incrimination
(6)	Protection of self-respect and dignity
(7)	Freedom of movement etc
(8)	Freedom of assembly
(9)	Freedom of association
(10) Freedom of trade, business and profession
(11)	Freedom of speech and writing
(12) Freedom to practice religion and manage religious institutions
(13) Protection from paying taxes for the promotion of a particular religion
(14) Reservations related to educational institutions about religion etc
(15) Rulings about property
(16) Protection of property rights
(17) Equality with citizens
(18) Non-discrimination regarding entry to public places
(19) Every citizen is protected against discrimination in employment.
(20) Every citizen has the right to promote his own language, script and culture and to establish institutions for the same.
5. Policy principles to guide institutions of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan
Incorporation of policy principles into constitutions began with the Constitution of Spain.
In 1937, the principles of the policy were also included in the constitution of Ireland.
These principles were also included in the Constitution of India. The principles of the policy were also defined in the previous constitutions of Pakistan.
In fact, the practice of including the principles of policy in the constitution is necessary for a new political system, the reason being that within any new system, the achievement of multiple objectives is not immediately possible, but for this, the conditions must first be favorable. It is necessary .
Principles of policy indicate the objectives and basic principles with which the business of the state will be conducted.
All the institutions of the state formulate their policies in the light of these objectives.
These principles are also included in the Constitution of Pakistan (1973).
These principles provide a blueprint for determining future paths.
These principles are general in nature and their violation cannot be challenged in court.
As these principles reflect the spirit and mood of the Constitution, courts cannot ignore them while interpreting the Articles of the Constitution.
In the words of former Law Minister and prominent intellectual Mr. AK Brohi (deceased), their position is the manual of the country's government. They mark the basic ideas of the country's policy which the government and legislature have to implement.
It is the responsibility of every institution and authority of the state to follow these principles of the policy while performing their duties.
However, the implementation of these principles is dependent on the availability of resources for this purpose.
Implementation Report: Every year the President on the affairs of the Federation and the Governor of each province on the affairs of his province shall prepare a report on the implementation and compliance of the principles of the policy. The President will submit a report to the National Assembly and the Governor to the Provincial Assembly.
No action or the validity of any law shall be challenged on the ground that it is not in accordance with the principles of policy nor shall any action be maintainable against the State, any agency of the State or any person on that ground.
The policy principles to guide the State institutions will be as follows:
(1)	Islamic Way of Life: Steps will be taken to enable the Muslims of Pakistan, individually and collectively, to organize their lives in accordance with the basic principles and fundamental concepts of Islam and to provide them with facilities that will enable them to read the Qur'an. And understand the meaning of life according to the Sunnah.
(2)	Regarding the Muslims of Pakistan, the State shall endeavor to:
(a)	Making the teaching of the Holy Quran and Islam compulsory; To encourage and facilitate the learning of the Arabic language and to arrange for the correct and proper printing and publication of the Holy Qur'an.
(b) promote unity and adherence to Islamic ethical standards; And
(c) Organizing regular organization of Zakat, Ushar, Awqaf and mosques.
(3)	Promotion of local bodies: The State shall encourage local bodies consisting of elected representatives of the respective areas and special representation shall be given to farmers, laborers and women in such bodies.
(4)	Discouragement of regional and other similar prejudices: The State shall discourage regional, ethnic, tribal, communal and provincial prejudices among its citizens.
(5)	Involvement of Women in National Life: Steps will be taken to ensure full participation of women in all spheres of national life.
(6)	The state will protect marriage, family, mother and child.
(7)	Protection of Minorities: The State shall protect the legitimate rights and interests of minorities.
They will have adequate representation in federal and provincial jobs.
(8)	Promotion of social justice: The government will take special care of the educational and economic interests of the backward classes and regions.
Compulsory and free education will be provided to all citizens to the extent possible.
The doors of higher education shall be equally open to all citizens provided they fulfill the required conditions.
Adequate steps will be taken to provide speedy adjudication of cases and affordable justice in the judicial system.
Hours of work shall be fixed in factories and other establishments and full care shall be taken to ensure that women and children are not subjected to undue labour.
People belonging to all regions of the country will be provided with enough facilities in educational, agricultural and industrial fields so that they can play an effective role in all areas of national life.
(9)	It will decentralize powers as far as possible in government departments for the sake of better administration and public convenience.
(10) Elimination of social evils: Prostitution, gambling, use of intoxicating drinks and harmful drugs, obscene literature and advertisements shall be prevented.
(11)	 Social and Economic Welfare: Will raise the standard of living of the common man.
It will seek to end the distribution of wealth and resources and the concentration of production.
Efforts will be made to achieve the welfare of the people irrespective of gender, caste, religion or race by guaranteeing fair distribution of rights between owners and workers in factories and between landlords and farmers in the field of agriculture. Social security will be provided to all employed persons.
Destitute persons will be supported. Pakistan's employment income will be reduced.
(12) Joining the Armed Forces of the People: The State shall enable the people of all regions of Pakistan to join the Armed Forces of Pakistan.
(13) Strengthening ties with the world of Islam and promoting international peace: The state will try to maintain and strengthen the brotherly relations between Muslim countries on the basis of Islamic unity.
To support the common interests of the peoples of Asia, Africa and Latin America, to promote international peace and security, and to promote goodwill and friendly relations among all nations, and to encourage the peaceful settlement of international disputes. Be encouraged.
The actual implementation of policy-making principles depends largely on an effective and informed public opinion.
If the national mass media and the conscious section of the people are interested in the implementation of these theoretical principles of the constitution, then these principles can have the same status as the constitutional traditions in the British system.
The implementation of these customs is also effective and due to the conscious public opinion.
Chapter 2
Federation of Pakistan
1. Federal Republic
According to Article No. 1 of the Constitution, Pakistan shall be a federal republic named
"Islamic Republic of Pakistan" will be.
2. Areas of Pakistan
The territories of Pakistan shall consist of:
(a)	Provinces: Balochistan, Punjab, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa, and Sindh;
(b) the capital region of Islamabad;
(c) Federally Administered Tribal Areas; And
(d)	 States and territories which are or may become part of Pakistan by accession or otherwise.
Note: The Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament) may, by law, admit new states or territories into the Federation on such terms and conditions as it deems fit.

3. Principal Institutions of the Federation
A modern state exercises the following powers:
(a)	Legislation
(2)	Enforcing laws, making proposals for new laws, executive powers
(3)	 Interpreting the law and applying the law to individual cases
In order to exercise the above powers, a modern state has three basic institutions and the constitution specifies the principles and procedures of relationship between these institutions.

There are three basic institutions of the state at the federal level in the Islamic Republic of Pakistan.
(1)	Legislature: Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament), which consists of the President and two chambers, the Senate and the National Assembly.
(2)	Administration: Federal Government; Administration of tribal areas under federation and administration of regional capital Islamabad
(3)	 Judiciary: Supreme Court (Supreme Court of Pakistan)
The jurisdiction of the Supreme Court has been extended to the Federally Administered Tribal Areas (FATA).

Administrative structure of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan
Chapter 3
President of the State
1. Head of the Federal Republic
According to the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, the Federal Republic of Pakistan shall have a President who shall be the Head of State and shall represent the unity of the Republic.
He shall be a Muslim, his age shall be at least 45 years and he shall be eligible to be elected as a member of the National Assembly.
According to the procedure written in the Second Schedule of the Constitution, the electoral body consisting of the members of both the Houses and the Provincial Assemblies will elect the President of the State. Before taking office, the Chief Justice of Pakistan will take oath on the text mentioned in the third schedule of the constitution.
Shall not hold any position of profit in the service of the President of Pakistan, nor shall he hold any other position entitling to compensation for services.
The President shall hold office for a period of five years.
A person holding the office of President shall be eligible for re-election to that office but no person shall hold office for more than two consecutive terms.
The President may resign from office by hand writing to the Speaker of the National Assembly.
2. Removal (or impeachment) of the President
The President may be removed from office on grounds of physical or mental incapacity or impeached on any charge of violation of the Constitution or gross misconduct, in accordance with the procedure laid down in Article 47 of the Constitution. .
At least half of the total membership of either House shall notify the Speaker of the National Assembly, or as the case may be, the Chairman of the Senate, of their intention to move a resolution for the removal, or as the case may be, of impeachment, of the President. may give notice in writing, and the said notice shall specify the particulars of the President's disqualification or the charge against him.
joint sitting of both the Houses shall inquire or cause to be inquired into the ground or allegation on which the notice is based.
The President shall have the right to appear or be represented before the joint session during the inquiry, if any.
If, as a result of the investigation, after deliberation, in a joint session, a resolution of at least two-thirds of the total membership of the Majlis Shura (Parliament) is passed to the effect that the President is not fit to assume office due to incapacity. or is guilty of violation of the Constitution or gross misconduct, the President shall immediately leave office upon the passing of the resolution.
3. Vacancy of the post of President
If the office of the President becomes vacant due to the death, resignation or impeachment of the President, the Chairman Senate or, if he is unable to perform the duties of the President, the Speaker of the National Assembly shall be the Acting President until such time as As per clause (3) of Article 41 of the Constitution no President is elected.
4. President's power to pardon etc
According to Article 45 of the Constitution, the President shall have the power to pardon, postpone and stay for a certain period of time and mitigate, suspend or commute the punishment given by any court, tribunal or other competent authority. .
5. Keeping the President informed on domestic and foreign policy matters and legislative proposals
According to Article 46 of the Constitution, the Prime Minister shall keep the President informed on all matters of internal and foreign policy and on all such legislative proposals that the Federal Government intends to bring before the Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament).
6. The President will act on the advice of the Prime Minister
(1) Under Article 48 of the Constitution, the President shall, in the exercise of his functions, act in accordance with the advice of the Cabinet (or the Prime Minister); However, within fifteen days of the receipt of the advice, the President may direct the Cabinet or the Prime Minister to reconsider such advice and the President may direct for reconsideration and the President may, after reconsideration, in accordance with the advice given “ Within ten days'' will act.
(2) The President shall, in relation to any matter in respect of which he is empowered to do so by the Constitution, act in his discretion and on the justification of anything which the President may do in his discretion for any reason. , no matter what, will not be objected.
7. Supervisory Cabinet
On the completion of its term of office of the Assembly or on its dissolution under Article 58, the President shall appoint the Caretaker Cabinet.
However, the President will select the Caretaker Prime Minister with the advice of the Prime Minister of the outgoing Assembly and the Leader of the Opposition. If the Prime Minister and the Leader of the Opposition do not agree on the appointment of a person as Caretaker Prime Minister, the provisions of Article 224 A shall be followed.
Chapter 4
federal government
1. The Prime Minister
The meeting of the National Assembly will be held on the 21st day after the general election of the Assembly, but the President can call the meeting earlier.
After the election of the Speaker and Deputy Speaker, the National Assembly shall elect one of its Muslim members as Prime Minister without any further proceedings.
The Prime Minister will be elected by the majority votes of the total members of the National Assembly.
This elected member will be invited by the President to assume the office of Prime Minister.
He shall take oath before the President of the State in the form of text mentioned in Schedule III before assuming office.
There will be no restriction on the number of terms of office of the Prime Minister. The Prime Minister will hold office during the pleasure of the President.
When the President is satisfied that the Prime Minister does not have the confidence of the majority of the members of the National Assembly, he will call a meeting of the National Assembly and ask the Prime Minister to obtain a vote of confidence from the Assembly. The Prime Minister may submit his resignation in writing to the President. The President may ask the Prime Minister to remain in office until his successor is appointed as Prime Minister.
No confidence against the Prime Minister
The National Assembly can pass a motion of no confidence against the Prime Minister which is presented by at least twenty percent members of the total membership of the National Assembly.
No vote shall be taken before the expiration of a period of three days or after a period of seven days from the day on which the said resolution is presented to the National Assembly.
No no-confidence motion against the Prime Minister shall not be presented in the National Assembly while the National Assembly is considering the demands presented in the annual balance sheet.
If the motion of no confidence against the Prime Minister is passed by a majority of the total membership of the National Assembly, the Prime Minister shall not continue to hold office.
2. Cabinet
There will be a Cabinet of Ministers headed by the Prime Minister to assist and advise the President in carrying out his duties.
The Cabinet including the Ministers of State shall collectively be accountable to the Senate and the National Assembly. (Article 91 of the Constitution of Pakistan)
3. Federal Ministers and Ministers of State
The President shall, on the advice of the Prime Minister, appoint the Federal Ministers and Ministers of State from among the members of the Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament); Provided that the number of Federal Ministers and Ministers of State who are members of the Senate shall not at any time exceed one-fourth of the number of Federal Ministers. Before assuming office, a Federal Minister or a Minister of State shall take an oath before the President in the text given in the Third Schedule of the Constitution. A federal minister or a minister of state may resign from his office by writing under his signature to the President or the President may dismiss him from office on the advice of the Prime Minister.
Minister who has not been a Member of the National Assembly for six consecutive months shall cease to be a Minister at the end of the said period and shall not be re-appointed a Minister before the dissolution of that Assembly unless he is elected a Member of the Assembly.
However, this condition shall not apply to a member of the Senate and this condition shall not disqualify the Prime Minister or a Federal Minister or a Minister of State from continuing in office during any period when the National Assembly is dissolved. This condition cannot and will not prevent any person from being appointed as Prime Minister or Federal Minister or Minister of State during any such period.
4. Counselors
The President, on the advice of the Prime Minister, may appoint up to five advisers on such terms as he may determine.
5. Special Assistants
There will be a special assistant or special assistants to the Prime Minister whose rank and duties will be determined by the Prime Minister.
6. Attorney General
The state has an Attorney General, who is the highest law officer of the state.
The Constitution of Pakistan empowers the President to appoint a person who is qualified to be a judge of the Supreme Court as the Attorney General of Pakistan.
It shall be the duty of the Attorney General to advise the Federal Government on such legal matters and to perform such other duties of a legal nature as may be assigned to him by the Federal Government and in the performance of his duties he shall have all the powers of Pakistan. Right to be heard in courts and tribunals.
Under the Constitution of Pakistan, the Attorney General has the right to participate in the proceedings of any House of the Majlis Shura (Parliament) or any of its committees, but does not have the right to vote because he is not a member of the Majlis Shura (Parliament).
According to the Rules of Procedure 1973, no Division shall consult the Attorney General except through the Law and Justice Division and in accordance with the procedures laid down by that Division.
If there is a difference of opinion between the Attorney General and the Law and Justice Division, the matter will be submitted to the Minister of Law and Justice for his opinion.
If the Minister disagrees with the Attorney General, the matter will be referred to the Prime Minister for orders.
7. Executive authority of the Federation
Under the Constitution, the executive power of the Federation shall apply to matters in respect of which the Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament) has the power to make laws.
These matters include the exercise of rights, authority and jurisdiction over territories in and outside Pakistan; Provided that the aforesaid power shall not, unless expressly contained in the Constitution or in any law enacted by the Majlis-i-Shura (Parliament), apply in any province to any matter in respect of which the Provincial Assembly There will be power to make laws.
8. Exercise of administrative authority
The administrative authority of the federation, the federal government consisting of the prime minister and the federal ministers, will be exercised in the name of the president.
The federal government will perform its duties through the prime minister.
The prime minister will be the chief administrator of the federation. The Prime Minister shall act directly or through the Federal Ministers to perform his functions.
On the recommendation of the federal government, the Majlis-e-Shura (Parliament) can assign functions to the officers or subordinate bodies of the federal government through law (Article 98 of the Constitution of Pakistan).
9. Carrying out the work of the Federal Government
According to Article 90 of the Constitution, all administrative actions of the federal government are carried out in the name of the President.
Under the Constitution, the Federal Government is empowered to prescribe by rules the manner of validating orders and other documents made or issued in the name of the President and the validity of any order or document so validated in any court. No objection shall be entertained on the ground that it was not framed or promulgated by the President. According to Article 99 of the Constitution, the federal government is also responsible for making rules for the distribution and performance of its functions.
10. Rules, 1973
In exercise of the powers conferred by Articles 90 and 99 of the Constitution, the Federal Government framed the Rules, 1973 for the distribution and performance of its functions, which came into force on 14th August, 1973. These rules include the formation and organization of ministries/divisions at the federal level and their list, distribution between divisions, consultation in divisions, procedure of approaching the Prime Minister and the President, procedure of the cabinet, procedure of legislation. , relations with the Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament), relations with the provinces, procedures for taking measures in emergency situations and miscellaneous measures.
Chapter 5
Federal Government Offices
1. Division
At the federal level, government affairs are handled by ministries/divisions. "Division" means a comprehensive administrative unit, which is responsible for carrying out the work of the Federal Government within a clear and specific scope. A 'proclamation' is formally issued by the federal government to grant the status of a division to an administrative unit and it is entered in Schedule I of the Rules, 1973.
2. Ministry
In the dictionary, ministry refers to the minister's department, portfolio or department of the ministry. In the United Kingdom, the term is used for a government department for which a minister is responsible to Parliament. The administrative unit at the federal level in Pakistan is a division and a ministry refers to "a division or group of divisions". The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has only one division i.e. Foreign Affairs Division while the Ministry of Finance, Revenue, Economic Affairs, Statistics and Privatization consists of four divisions (Finance Division, Revenue Division, Economic Affairs Division and Privatization Division).
Ministry of Finance, Revenue, Economic Affairs, Statistics and Privatization
Finance Division	Revenue Division	Economic Affairs Division		Privatization Division
3. Federal Secretariat
The divisions and ministries are collectively called the Federal Secretariat. The Federal Secretariat consists of the Ministries and Divisions listed in Schedule I of the Rules, 1973. Whenever necessary, the Prime Minister may form a new ministry comprising more or more divisions.
The Prime Minister divides the work of the federal government among his ministers by placing one or more divisions under the custody of one minister from among the divisions listed in Schedule I. The division or ministry, which is not assigned to any Minister, shall be under the custody of the Prime Minister. The Prime Minister can assign more than one division to a minister.
4. Affiliated Deptt
Adjunct Departments of each Division are established as necessary to provide expert advice on technical aspects of policy issues and to implement the policy formulated by the Government.
These subsidiary departments work directly under their respective divisions and their creation is regularly announced in the Government Gazette.
In the third schedule of the Rules, 1973, the name of the attached department is added. For example, the details of the departments attached to the Personnel Division are listed below:
(1)	Staff Welfare Organization, Islamabad.
(2)	Secretariat Training Institute, Islamabad.
(3)	Federal Public Service Commission, Islamabad.
(4)	Akhtar Hameed Khan National Center for Rural Development
5. Subordinate Office
An office of the federal government other than a ministry, division or affiliated department. It usually works under an affiliated department within a specific scope and provides basic and technical information to that department.
Advises the attached department on the technical aspects of a particular problem related to his scope and implements the government policy in the field under the general direction of the attached department (or the division itself).
6. Autonomous/Semi-Autonomous Institutions
These institutions are established by an Act of the Majlis-e-Shoora (Parliament) or as a Public Limited Company or under the Trust Act. These institutions carry out different types of activities:
(1) Commercial, semi-commercial, industrial and business establishments: Trading Corporation of Pakistan; Heavy Industries, Taxila; Pakistan Aeronautical Complex Kamra; Pakistan Arms Factory, Wow; Pakistan Security Printing Corporation; Pasco; PIA, etc.
(2) Regulatory bodies: OGRA, NEPRA, PEMRA etc.
(3) Service Delivery Institutions: Federal Board of Secondary and Higher Secondary Education, Islamabad; National Logistics Cell (NLC); Pimms etc
(4) Institutions for the promotion of specific objectives: these institutions promote knowledge and culture, cultural traditions, domestic products and employment and tourism; For example, Iqbal Academy, Quaid-i-Azam Academy, Folk Heritage, National Book Foundation, Pakistan Sports Board, Investment Board, Pakistan Development Tourism Corporation, Overseas Employment Corporation, Pakistan Industrial Development Corporation etc.
(5) Financial, banking etc. institutions: Pakistan Insurance Corporation; Pakistan Kuwait Investment Company; Agricultural Development Bank; National Bank of Pakistan etc.
(6) Training Institutions: Federal Judicial Academy; Civil Services Academy Lahore, Pakistan Audit and Accounts Academy Lahore, Foreign Service Academy Islamabad etc.
(7) Development Institutions: Khushal Pakistan Fund; Pakistan Housing Authority etc.
Chapter 6
Determinants between divisions
1. Clear and specific scope
The execution of government affairs at the federal level is the responsibility of the divisions.
clear and specific scope of official work has been laid down for each division. In Schedule II of the Rules, 1973, the work assigned to each division has been separately detailed.
An example of a staff division is given to illustrate the work assigned to divisions.
2. Example of staff division
The Staff Division is one of the two divisions of the Bina Secretariat
The main function of the Personnel Division is the regulation of all matters that apply to civil posts related to federal affairs.
3. Scope of Personnel Division
This division serves as the primary office for the staff.
Recruitment, promotion, career planning, capacity building, verification of character and experience of employees, conduct and discipline and terms and conditions of employment (including re-employment after retirement) of employees, except those prescribed by the Ministry. Handles matters related to finance.
Responsible for formulating professional groups and formulating policy and managing the four professional groups.
These groups include Secretariat Group, Pakistan Administrative Service, Police Service Pakistan and Office Management Group/Office Management Group.
4. Guidelines for Personnel Division
In order to achieve its objectives, the Personnel Division is guided by the following rules:
(a)	The Civil Servants Act, 1973
(b) Service Tribunal Act, 1973
(c) Federal Public Service Commission Ordinance, 1977
5. Professional training
A major responsibility of the Personnel Division is to administer training in the field of public administration.
Training institutes have been established for professional training of civil servants at various levels.
These training institutions include National School of Public Policy, Lahore; National Institute of Management, Karachi; Quetta, Lahore and Peshawar; These include National Management College, Lahore, Academy for Rural Development Peshawar, Civil Services Academy, Lahore and Secretariat Training Institute, Islamabad. The main objective of imparting training in these institutes is to build the capacity of the employees in professional matters so that they can be prepared for higher responsibilities and can adequately face the daily challenges in the modern world.
6. Administrative services
The Staff Division through its Department of Administrative Services acts as an administrative adviser to the Federal Government and studies various cases to solve special administrative problems and uses modern administrative techniques for this purpose.
These techniques include Program Evaluation and Evaluation (PEART), Critical Methodology (CPM), Systems Analysis and Operations Research and Organization and Methodology (O&M).
The responsibilities of this department include the following:
(1)	review the organization, functions and procedures of divisions, affiliated departments, offices and departments of the federal government, autonomous bodies and industries taken under the administrative authority of the government to improve their efficiency;
(2)	reorganization of a division or affiliated department or change of status of an affiliated department;
(3)	Periodical review of the staff strength of divisions, affiliated departments and all other offices of the Federal Government;
(4)	To make recommendations to simplify the rules, forms and procedures for effective and efficient conduct of public affairs so as to reduce public anxiety and develop mandatory safeguards against corruption.
(5)	 Training of government officials in Pakistan and abroad in Organization and Methodology (O&M), Critical Methodology (CPM), Program Evaluation and Evaluation (PEART) techniques, systems analysis and operational research.
(6)	Promoting the use of knowledge and organization and method (O&M) concepts, critical methodologies, evaluation and evaluation program techniques, systems analysis and operational research in all government offices and institutions.
(7)	Idea Award Scheme
(8)	Public Administration Research Center Pakistan
(9)	Organization on a permanent basis of a working unit other than a section in a division
(10) Determination of status of government offices
(11)	Pooling of surplus staff of federal civil servants and arrangements for their deployment in government offices
7. Welfare staff
Personnel Division also looks after the welfare of civil servants and their dependents. Two subsidiary departments (Organization of Staff Welfare and Federal Employees Welfare Fund and Group Insurance) serve for this purpose.
8. Miscellaneous Responsibilities
The responsibilities of the Personnel Division also include the following:
(1) Matters relating to the following:
(a) Central Selection Board;
(b) Special Selection Boards, except such Special Selection Boards as may be constituted in the respective Divisions relating to the selection of officers for appointment to Pakistani diplomatic missions abroad;
(c) Selection Committee for provincial posts related to All Pakistan Unified Grades;
(2)	Professional planning
(a) instructions regarding the preparation and maintenance of performance appraisal reports of Government servants;
(b) central arrangements for arranging two sets of original or duplicate performance appraisal reports of officers;
(3)	Administrative reforms
(4)	Administration of the Civil Servants Act, 1973 and the rules made thereunder
(5)	Service Tribunal Act, 1973
(6)	Accidental leave
(7)	Office Hours
(8)	Uniforms of Government Servants
(9)	 Association of Federal Employees Policy Issues
(10) Sanction of rank to non-secretariat officers
9. Head Departments of Staff Division
The Staff Division is divided into the following Head Departments (Wings) to carry out the assigned tasks:
(1)	Professional Planning Wing
(2)	Training Wing
(3)	Disciplinary and Prosecution Wing
(4)	Regulation Wing
(5)	Administrative Services Wing
(6)	Staff Wing
(7)	Administration Wing
