11. Attached Department of Personnel Division (Staff Welfare Organization)
An affiliated department of the Staff Division is the Staff Welfare Organization, Islamabad. It was established in 1951 as a section of the Staff Division. Later it was made a separate department.
12. Featured Activities
Quran education for federal employees and their dependents.
Scholarships for Education of Children of Government Servants.
Financial assistance in case of death or illness of Government servants or in case of visual impairment.
Provision of ambulance service and mortuary vehicle.
Provision of accommodation at health facilities, hostel facility for accommodation of working women.
Child care facility for working women.
Training in Typing, Shorthand, Computer etc. for Government Servants and their dependents.
Facilitation of community centers for various social, cultural, religious and recreational activities as well as healthy activities and sports facilities for government employees and their dependents.
Chapter 7
Organization of Divisions and Division of Work
1. Official Head of Division
Each Division has a Secretary (the term includes General Secretary, Principal Secretary, Acting Secretary, Additional Secretary or Giant Secretary-in-charge) and other officers under him. A single person may be in charge of more than one division.
The Secretary is the official head of the division.
2. Wings
Each division is divided into Head Departments (Wings) each Head Department (Wing) is headed by Giant Secretary / Senior Giant Secretary.
(Additional Secretaries are also appointed between the Secretary and the Giant Secretary in larger divisions) There are two or more Deputy Secretaries under the Giant Secretary.
There are usually two or more sections under each Deputy Secretary.
3. Sections
A Section (Sygha) is the basic administrative unit of each Division constituted according to the criteria laid down by the Staff Division (Administrative Services Wing).
Section Officer (Scale 17/18) is in charge of the section.
4. Extraordinary administrative unit
If the structure of a unit does not conform to the section, it may be organized in a manner other than section on a permanent basis in consultation with the Staff Division.
In case of creation of an unusual unit like Research Cell, the Staff Division is informed.
Division of work in division
5. Responsibilities of the Secretary (in light of the Secretariat's instructions)
(1)	Being the head of the Ministry/Division, the Secretary is responsible for its effective management and discipline.
He is also responsible for the execution of official work in accordance with the Secretariat of Government Affairs and instructions assigned to the Division under the Rules, 1973.
(2)	It is the responsibility of the Secretary to ensure that the matters presented to the Minister-in-Charge, Prime Minister, President or the Cabinet are complete.
(3)	It is the responsibility of the Secretary to delegate powers to his subordinates and in doing so to determine the maximum extent of those powers; Issue clear standing orders based on these powers and lay down procedures for dealing with matters in the Division.
(4)	The Secretary shall ensure that the distribution in the division is fair; Matters should be presented vertically, not horizontally; And in the course of proceedings, no case, including the Secretary, should normally pass through more than two stages.
(5)	The Secretary shall review the powers delegated to various officers from time to time to ensure maximum delegation of authority at the primary and intermediate levels to deal with matters.
He shall devise a proper system to keep himself fully abreast of the affairs of the Division.
6. Assignment of duties to Additional Secretary/Giant Secretary
The Secretary will assign duties within a very clear scope to the Additional Secretaries and Joint Secretaries working under him.
The officers concerned within their jurisdiction will take full responsibility and submit the matters directly to the Minister in-charge for orders.
These matters will be returned to the concerned officer through the Secretary so that the Secretary is informed.
The Secretary has the power to call for his consideration any matter assigned to him.
He may also direct that the Minister be consulted on a particular matter before submitting it to him.
7. Authority of the Deputy Secretary
The Deputy Secretary shall deal with all matters not involving major policy issues; He is empowered to deal with matters under the rules or standing orders.
8. Authority of Section Officer/Officer Saygha
The Section Officer (Afsir Saygha) will deal with all such cases where there are clear norms and there is no problem of deviation from these norms; He is empowered to deal with those matters under the rules or standing orders. In case of any doubt he may take instructions from his superior.
Chapter 8
An engineer in the federal government
1. General Instructions
No important policy decision in the federal government will be taken without the approval of the Prime Minister.
policy decision taken by the Prime Minister shall not be altered or violated without consulting the Prime Minister.
2. Responsibility of Minister
It will be the duty of the Minister to assist the Prime Minister in formulating policy.
He shall be responsible for the policy relating to his division and shall inform the Prime Minister of any important matter which he has dealt with without consulting the Prime Minister.
The Minister-in-charge will be responsible for following up the affairs of the division in the National Assembly.
3. Responsibilities of Secretary (in light of Rules, 1973)
(l) Duties of Secretary (in relation to Minister-in-Charge)
Shall assist the Minister in-charge of the Division in formulation of policy and duly implement the approved policy.
He shall submit to the BINA all proposals for legislation with the approval of the Minister. The work of the Division should ordinarily be dealt with by the authority or with the permission of the Minister-in-charge.
He shall apprise the Minister-in-charge of the general performance of the Division and any important matter which has been dealt with without reference to the Minister.
(b) Principal Accounting Officer
The Secretary shall be the Principal Accounting Officer of the Division, Affiliated Departments and Subordinate Offices and shall ensure that the funds placed at his disposal are spent in accordance with the rules laid down by the Ministry of Finance.
(c) Issuance of Permanent Orders
The Ruler shall, subject to the provisions of the Rules, 1973, and with the approval of the Minister in charge, issue such standing orders as may prescribe the manner of dealing with matters in the Division, including the division of work among the officers of the Division, and in such orders shall specify the nature of such matters or matters. It has been specified that his subordinate officer will deal with it.
(d) Obligation of Rules 1973
He shall be responsible for the scrupulous observance of these rules and where he considers that any significant deviation from these rules, whether in his own division or in any other division, is taking place, he shall bring the matter to the notice of the Minister in charge. will bring
(h) Referral of matters to Minister-in-Charge
When the Secretary submits a matter to the Minister, the Minister can approve or reject the suggestions or opinions of the Secretary.
The Secretary shall generally pass on the decision of the Minister and implement it.
(f) Procedure in case of disagreement between the Secretary and the Minister
If the Secretary feels that the Minister's decision is manifestly wrong and would cause grave injustice or undue hardship, he shall refer the matter back to the Minister, giving reasons.
If the Minister still maintains his first decision and the matter is important enough, he will request the Minister to refer the matter to the Prime Minister for orders.
If the matter is not referred to the Prime Minister, the Secretary-in-charge will submit it directly to the Prime Minister with the views of the Minister-in-charge.
4. Verbal orders
Verbal orders of an officer of the Government shall be recorded as usual and presented to the issuing sovereign.
If time permits, confirmation of orders will be obtained before proceeding. However, when action is required immediately under exigencies or if it is not possible to obtain written confirmation of the orders before commencing the action, the officer to whom the oral orders have been given shall take the required action and as soon as he has the opportunity to The issuer shall submit the report to the competent authority and obtain the required approval.
5. Interpretation of Rules 1973
If any doubt or dispute arises in the interpretation of these rules or in determining to which Division a matter properly belongs, the matter shall be referred to the Cabinet Division whose decision shall be final.
The Cabinet Division will obtain orders from the Prime Minister where necessary.
Whenever necessary, supplementary instructions related to these rules will be issued by the Cabinet Division, however, special or general orders framed by the Divisions under these rules will be issued by the concerned Division after consultation with the Division.
6. Issuance of order against law/policy
If any order issued is against any law, rule or policy, it is the duty of the next subordinate officer to point out the same to the superior authority issuing the order.
7. Individual and collective responsibility
For the opinions sent to the President or the administrative orders issued in the name of the President, whether by the Minister alone or as a result of the decision of the Cabinet, the Minister shall be collectively responsible, but the principal of the work dealt with in his portfolio. The minister will accept the responsibility.
8. Orders and documents, agreements and contracts
(1)	Under Article 173 of the Constitution, all the administrative actions of the federal government will be assumed in the name of the President.
Note: In relation to provincial governments, the words "Federal Government" and in relation to foreign governments, "Government of Pakistan" will be appropriate.
(2)	 The officers listed in Schedule IV of the Rules of Procedure, 1973 can attest with their signatures the orders issued in the name of the President and the documents executed. However, in certain cases, an officer may be authorized by the order of the Prime Minister for a specific occasion.
(3)	The Foreign Affairs Division will issue instructions regarding the procedure for validating orders and documents in connection with the representation of Pakistan in foreign countries or in international conferences and in international agreements and treaties.
(4)	The Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs Division shall issue instructions on contracts entered into by the President and on the performance of such contracts and all insurances relating to propert
Chapter 9
Mutual consultation across divisions
1. General Instructions
When the subject of a matter concerns more than one Division, the Division In-charge shall be responsible for consultation with the other concerned Division. Before issuing any order or placing any matter before the Cabinet or the Prime Minister, all the concerned divisions will consider the matter and give their opinion.
Such consultation shall be held as soon as practicable.
In cases of extreme urgency, with the approval of the Prime Minister, this requirement may be waived but thereafter the matter shall be brought to the notice of other concerned divisions as soon as possible.
2. Committee of Secretaries
There will be a Committee of Secretaries to consider matters referred by a Division, Minister or Prime Minister to utilize the experience and collective wisdom of senior officers on the subject under consideration. If the Secretary of a Division agrees to a proposal in a matter considered by the Committee of Secretaries, it shall not be necessary to consult his Division again on the proposal.
3. Instructions for consultation with specific divisions
Detailed instructions have been issued in the Rules, 1973 for consultation with the following Divisions:
(1)	Cabinet Division
(2)	Personnel Division
(3)	 Finance Division
(4)	Law and Justice Division
(5)	External Affairs Division
(6)	 Revenue Division
4. Consultation with Cabinet Division
(1)	No Federal Ministry/Division shall issue or be empowered to issue such orders without prior consultation with the Cabinet Division which include the following matters:
(a)	 Interpretation of Rules, 1973;
(b) change in appointment between different divisions of the Ministry;
(c) the number of personal staff and the terms and conditions of employment of Ministers, Ministers of State, Special Assistants to the Prime Minister and other high officials of rank and status equivalent to Ministers or Ministers of State; And
(d)	Selection of Assistant Director and Deputy Director level officer in Intelligence Bureau
(2)	Under Clause (1) of Article 145 of the Constitution, the proposals of instructions given by the President to a Provincial Governor shall be submitted to the President by the concerned Division, but a copy of the Presidential Decree shall be provided to the Cabinet Division.
(3)	The respective Divisions shall seek approval from the Cabinet Division for proposals to send delegations to foreign countries which are not in accordance with the procedure laid down by the Division regarding the classification of International Conferences.
5. Consultation with Personnel Division
(1)	No Ministry/Division shall, without prior consultation with the Staff Division, issue or authorize the issue of orders other than those issued under general or special powers conferred on the Staff Division in respect of the following matters:
(1)	appointment to a post in basic scale pay 20 and above or equivalent whether by initial appointment or by promotion or transfer;
(2)	 Changes in terms and conditions of employment of federal civil servants;
(3)	 Altering the constitutional rights and privileges of a federal public servant;
(4)	 Expenditure proposals relating to the Finance Division under Rule 12 of the Rules, 1973;
(5)	Interpret the rules and regulations formulated by the Personnel Division, and
(6)	 Rules for recruitment to any post or post including the issue of withdrawal of any post or post from the jurisdiction of the Federal Public Service Commission for recruitment purposes.
6. Consultation with Finance Division
No Division shall, without the prior approval of the Finance Division, authorize the issuance of orders, except orders issued under general or specially delegated powers, which directly or indirectly affect the finances of the Federation. being or relating specifically to the following:
(1)	relinquishment, waiver or assignment of or guarantee of actual or potential benefits;
(2)	Expenditures for which there is no provision in the budget or which are not approved;
(3)	issuance of loans;
(4)	 reclassification of funds within the balance sheet;
(5)	 A change in the method of preparation of calculations or estimates of the balance sheet;
(6)	Receipt or expenditure of foreign exchange unless already allocated;
(7)	Changes in the terms and conditions of employment with regard to the statutory rights and privileges of public servants, which have financial implications;
(8)	 Interpretation of rules framed by Finance Division;
Any proposal requiring the prior concurrence of the Finance Division shall not be processed unless the Finance Division declines to give its consent.
If the Minister of the concerned Division does not agree with the Finance Minister and insists on his proposal, he will submit his proposal to the Prime Minister or if the Prime Minister so desires, he will submit it to the Cabinet.
When the details are not furnished with the proposal, formal orders will not be issued until the Finance Division submits its scrutiny report on the details of the proposal.
Except where powers are delegated to the Divisions under the rules framed by the Finance Division, every order of the Administrative Division authorizing the execution of the audit shall be forwarded to the audit authorities through the Ministry of Finance. will
7. Consultation with Revenue Division
Except for general or special powers delegated by the Division of Revenue, no Division shall, without prior consultation with the Division of Revenue, issue or authorize the issuance of orders that directly or indirectly affect federal taxes, levies, duties, Influence the collection of cess (local revenue) or revenue from fees.
8. Consultation with Foreign Affairs Division
In compliance with the general or special orders assigned by the Foreign Affairs Division, the Foreign Affairs Division shall be consulted on all matters affecting the foreign policy of Pakistan or the conduct of its foreign relations.
9. Consultation with Law and Justice, Human Rights and Parliamentary Affairs Division
Law and Justice, Human Rights and Parliamentary Affairs Division will be consulted in the following matters:
(1)	on all legal questions arising on a matter;
(2)	 on the interpretation of any law;
(3)	 Before issuing or authorizing the issuance of any order, rule, regulation, bye-law, proclamation, etc., in exercise of constitutional authority;
(4)	before commencing any criminal or civil proceedings in any court of law, involving the Government;
(5)	At the earliest possible stage when criminal or civil proceedings are instituted against the Government; And
(6)	Before the appointment of legal counsel in a division or any office or corporation under its administrative control; The Law, Justice, Human Rights and Parliamentary Affairs Division will make its recommendations after consultation with the Attorney General.
2. No Division shall consult with the Attorney General except through the Law and Justice, Human Rights and Parliamentary Affairs Division and in accordance with the procedures established by that Division.
If there is a difference of opinion between the Attorney General and the Law and Justice Division, the matter will be submitted to the Minister of Law and Justice for his opinion.
If the Minister disagrees with the Attorney General, the matter shall be referred to the Prime Minister for orders, who may refer the matter to the Cabinet if he so desires.
4. In accordance with Rules 27 to 30 of the Rules of 1973, the Law and Justice Division shall be consulted for any proposed legislation.
5.	Draft laws or emergency laws received from provincial governments or governors for President's approval or instructions will be reviewed in the concerned division and submitted to the President through the Law and Justice Division.
Chapter 10
Matters for Prime Minister's approval
1. Guiding principles
No order shall be issued without the approval of the Prime Minister in the following cases:
(1) Major Policy Matters: Matters relating to major policy or deviation from major policy, including deviation from a previous decision of the Cabinet or the Prime Minister;
(2) Application of Article 145 and Article 149 of the Constitution: (Matters relating to the Governor and Provincial Government): Matters relating to instructions to the Governor under Article 145 and to the Provincial Government under Article 149 of the Constitution;
(3) International agreement/agreement relating to provincial jurisdiction: Cases in which it is proposed that the Federal Government take responsibility for the implementation of an international agreement/agreement on a subject related to provincial jurisdiction;
(4) Honors and Medals: Matters of honors, medals, in recognition of valor and academic distinction;
(5) Petitions to the Prime Minister: Matters relating to petitions addressed to the Prime Minister which are neither blocked nor approved for sending to the Prime Minister under the instructions.
(6) Petition for mercy from the President of the State: Matters related to petitions for mercy against the death penalty awarded by the courts, in which the special power of the President of the State to exercise pardon;
(7) Miscellaneous Matters:
(a) the matters specified in Schedule V A of the Rules, 1973;
(b) Matters given in Schedule V A of the Rules, 1973, relating to the sanction of a suit against the holder of an office.
2. Procedure for presentation of cases
The procedure for submitting matters to the Prime Minister is as follows:
(a) Summary for the Prime Minister: The case submitted to the Prime Minister for orders shall consist of a full, concise and objective summary stating the relevant facts and points for decision and prepared on the same lines as The rules for Cabinet Summary are set out in the Car except that only one copy shall be required which shall not be printed.
The summary shall include specific recommendations of the Minister in charge and shall be accompanied by a draft letter where appropriate.
(2) Orders of the Prime Minister in oral conversation: If in any matter the orders of the Prime Minister have been obtained in oral conversation from the Minister, Minister of State, Special Assistant to the Prime Minister, Deputy Chairman Planning Commission or any other officer of the Government, then the Minister A written note containing a brief record of the conversation and orders with the Prime Minister will be submitted to the Prime Minister's Secretariat (Public) for the information of the Prime Minister.
Chapter 11
Matters to be presented to the Cabinet
1. Description of matters
The following matters will be presented to the Cabinet:
(1)	Official or unofficial proposals for legislation, including draft laws on demand;
(2)	Proclamation and repeal of emergency laws;
(3)	Budget situation and proposals before submitting the annual balance sheet (budget) and supplemental balance sheet or supplemental balance sheet under Articles 80 and 84 of the Constitution;
(4)	Proposals for the imposition, abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any tax and the issuance of loans;
(5)	Reference to the Supreme Court for advice on any question of law under clause (1) of section 186;
(6)	Power generation and inter-provincial wiring;
(7)	proposals relating to negotiations with foreign countries; For example, exchange of diplomatic and trade representatives, treaties and agreements, visits by goodwill delegations, representation at international conferences and meetings;
Note: All proposals for making cultural or other compromises with a foreign country will first be submitted to the Cabinet for in-principle approval and actual negotiations will begin only after the proposal is approved by the Cabinet.
(8)	Important reports and documents to be presented in the Assembly or Senate.
(9)	matters relating to important political, economic and administrative policies;
Note: Matters of this nature will first be brought to the notice of the Prime Minister by the Minister-in-charge. The Prime Minister will decide whether any such matter should be presented to the Cabinet.
(10) Any matter in respect of which the Minister-in-charge is of the opinion that it is of such importance that it should be considered in the Cabinet.
(11)	Other matters required to be referred to the Cabinet under the Rules, 1973;
(12) Any matter regarding which the Prime Minister wishes to be presented to the Cabinet.
2. Authority of the Prime Minister
The Prime Minister has the power to give instructions on the procedure for dealing with a matter without presenting it to the Cabinet.
3. Method of dealing with Cabinet matters
Matters entrusted to the Cabinet shall be dealt with in the following manner:
(a)	through discussion in cabinet meetings; or
(b) by rotation between Ministers; or
(c) by discussion in a Cabinet Committee meeting;
However, the decisions of the Committee shall be ratified by the Cabinet unless otherwise authorized by the Cabinet.
The Secretary to the Cabinet shall indicate the manner of dealing with the matter under the general or special orders of the Prime Minister.
4. Cabinet Committees
Cabinet committees may be constituted and their terms of reference and terms of membership shall be determined by the Minister or the Prime Minister.
Such committees may be standing or special committees. They will be appointed to deal with one type of matters or a special matter.
5. Procedure for presentation of matters in Cabinet
(1) In all matters referred to the Cabinet, the Secretary of the concerned Division shall provide a concise, clear and printed summary of the matter containing the background and relevant facts, points for decision and recommendations of the Minister-in-Charge, the Cabinet Secretary. will send to
If the opinion of the Division differs from that of the Minister, both opinions shall be included in the summary.
(2) In the case of proposed legislation, in which the assent of the Cabinet is required in principle, the summary shall clearly state the important matters on which the legislation is to be enacted.
(3) The summary should be as complete as possible and not exceeding two typed pages and should include only such relevant papers as appendices as are necessary for a proper understanding of the matter.
The number of copies of the summary and the manner in which it shall be prepared shall be determined by the Cabinet Secretary.
(4) If the matter relates to more than one Division, the summary shall not be submitted to the Cabinet Division until it has been considered by all the Divisions concerned.
In case of disagreement among them, the points of disagreement shall be clearly stated in the abstract, a copy of which shall be forwarded by the presenting division to the other concerned division along with the transmission of the abstract to the Cabinet Division.
(5) All draft laws, emergency laws or orders shall be submitted to the Cabinet after scrutiny by the Ministry of Law and Justice and Parliamentary Affairs Division and no changes shall be made without consultation with the said Division.
(6) No matter shall be accepted for inclusion in the agenda of a meeting of the Cabinet unless it is received by the Secretary Cabinet at least seven full days before the meeting; However, if the matter is of urgent nature and has to be taken up at short notice, the concerned Secretary shall obtain the Prime Minister's approval for including the matter in the agenda before sending it to the Cabinet.
(7) It shall be the duty of the Cabinet Secretary to satisfy himself that the documents submitted by the concerned Secretary are complete and in proper form. He will remand the matter to fulfill the requirements of the rules. If the Cabinet Secretary is satisfied that the matter cannot be brought before the Cabinet, he will advise that the matter should be brought before the appropriate forum or the Prime Minister.
Chapter 12
Matters for approval of the President
1. Orders of the President on the advice of the Prime Minister
Irrespective of the fact that some articles have been placed in the Rules of Procedure 1973, where under any article of the Constitution the President of the State has to perform any function or issue orders or the special approval of the President of the State is required, the relevant division shall A summary of Amar will include a paragraph entitled "Summary for the Prime Minister".
The Prime Minister will give his advice and present the matter to the President. Once the President looks into the matter and approves it, it will be sent back to the Prime Minister.
The matters to which this sub-rule applies are specified in Schedule V of the Rules, 1973.
2. Discretionary orders of the President
In view of the fact that some articles have been placed in the Rules of 1973, where under any article of the Constitution the President of the State has to perform any office or issue any orders at his discretion, then the President of the State through the relevant Division Prime Minister. shall present the case in the form of a complete, comprehensive and objective summary entitled ``Summary for the President of the State'' setting out the relevant facts and points for decision and prepared on the same lines as `` The rules for 'Summary for Cabinet' are as laid down in 1973 except that only one copy is required which should not be printed.
However, this procedure will not be applicable where the President has sent a decision to the Prime Minister to issue orders in matters of his discretion.
The matters to which this sub-rule applies are specified in the Sixth Schedule to the Rules, 1973.
3. Matters for information
The matters and documents listed in the seventh schedule of the Rules of Procedure, 1973 will be submitted to the President for information.
Chapter 13
MISCELLANEOUS INSTITUTIONS
1. National Economic Council
Under Article 156 of the Constitution, the President will constitute a National Economic Council.
The Council consists of the Prime Minister (Chairman), Chief Ministers, one member nominated by the Chief Minister from each province and four members nominated by the Prime Minister.
For details see Part III (Relations and procedures between the Federation and the Provinces), Chapter 3.
2. National Finance Commission
A National Finance Commission has been constituted under Article 160 of the Constitution for distribution of revenue between the Federation and the provinces.
This commission consists of the Minister of Finance of the Federal Government, Ministers of Finance of the Provincial Governments and such other persons as may be appointed by the President after consultation with the Governors of the Provinces.
For details, see Part III (Relations and Procedures between Federation and Provinces) Chapter 4
3. Inter-Provincial Conference
(1) Under the instructions of the Prime Minister, the meeting of the Inter-Provincial Conference will be organized by the Inter-Provincial Liaison Division, which will be chaired by the Prime Minister.
(2) Only matters of great importance in the economic, social and administrative spheres which require policy decisions and mutual discussion between the Federal and Provincial Governments shall be presented in the Inter-Provincial Conference.
(3) One of the major objectives of this conference is to promote a common approach in policy formulation and implementation between the federal government and the provincial governments in all matters of national interest.
(4) The conference also discusses such policy issues proposed by the Provincial Governments as have economic, social or administrative implications for the country as a whole.
4. Common Interests Council
Council of Common Interests has been organized under Article 153 of the Constitution. The Council will be appointed by the President and this Council will consist of the Prime Minister (Chairman), the Chief Ministers of the provinces and three members of the Federal Government nominated by the Prime Minister. For details, see Part III (Relations and procedures between the Federation and the Provinces), Chapter 3.
Chapter 14
Islamic ideological Counsil
Article 227 of the Constitution states that all existing laws shall be made in accordance with the Islamic injunctions prescribed in the Qur'an and Sunnah and no such law shall be enacted which is contrary to the said injunctions.
Note: (1)	Applying this clause to the personal law of a Muslim sect, the phrase "Qur'an and Sunnah" will mean the Qur'an and Sunnah of the said sect.
(2)	Nothing shall affect the personal laws of non-Muslim citizens or their status as citizens.
1. Composition of the Council
The Council of Islamic Ideology shall consist of not less than eight and not more than twenty such members as may be appointed by the President from among persons having knowledge of the principles and philosophy of Islam as laid down in the Qur'an and Sunnah. Or to understand the economic, political, legal and administrative problems of Pakistan.
While appointing the members of the Islamic Council, the following matters shall be taken into consideration:
(1) As far as practicable, the various schools of thought should be represented in the Council
(2) At least two members shall be persons each of whom is or has been a Judge of the Supreme Court or any High Court.
(3) At least one-third of the members, each of whom has been engaged in Islamic research or teaching for a period of at least fifteen years, and
(4) At least one female member.
The President shall appoint one of the members of the Islamic Ideological Council as its Chairman. A member of the Council shall hold office for a term of three years.
The President or the Governor of a province, if he so desires or if 40 per cent of the total membership of a house or a provincial assembly so demands, shall consult the Council on any question whether any proposed law is contrary to the injunctions of Islam or not.
2. Executive office
The functionaries of the Islamic Council will be as follows;
(1) To recommend to the Majlis Shura (Parliament) and Provincial Assemblies such means and resources by which the Muslims of Pakistan can be motivated and encouraged to adapt their lives individually and collectively to the principles and concepts of Islam in all respects. Which have been determined in the Qur'an and Sunnah.
(2) To advise a House, a Provincial Assembly, the President or a Governor on any question referred to the Council as to whether a proposed law is contrary to Islamic injunctions or not.
(3) recommending measures by which existing laws may be brought into conformity with Islamic injunctions as well as recommending the stages through which the proposed measures should be implemented, and
(4) To guide the Majlis Shura (Parliament) and the Provincial Assemblies to edit such rules of Islam in a suitable form which can be legally enforced.
Chapter 15
Civil Jobs
1. Protection against discrimination in employment
Article 27 of the Constitution states that no discrimination shall be made against any citizen who is qualified for appointment in the employment of any other Pakistan, merely on the basis of race, religion, caste, sex, residence or place of birth. will not be tolerated; However, posts can be reserved for the people of a class or region for a maximum period of forty years from the date of promulgation of the Constitution so that they get adequate representation in the employment of Pakistan. Certain positions or jobs may be reserved for persons of one sex in the interests of the said employment, if the said positions or jobs require the performance of such duties and functions as may be adequately performed by persons of the other sex. may not be granted, but the under-representation of any class or region in the constitution of Pakistan shall be compensated in such manner as may be prescribed by an Act of the Majlis Shura (Parliament).
Any person in the aforesaid protection by any provincial government or any local or other competent body of a province before being appointed under that government or competent body in relation to any post or any kind of employment under the said government or competent body, There shall be no objection to the imposition of conditions relating to residence in this province for a maximum period of three years.
2. Appointment and conditions of employment in the employment of Pakistan
According to Article 240 of the Constitution, federal jobs, vacancies in connection with federal affairs and total Pakistan jobs shall be under or through an Act of the Majlis Shura (Parliament).
(Total Pakistan employment means a joint employment between the Federation and the Provinces which existed immediately before the date of commencement of the Constitution or which was established by an Act of the Majlis Shura (Parliament).)
3. Civil Employees Act 1973
The Majlis Shura (Parliament) passed the Civil Servants Act, 1973 to regulate the appointment of persons in the service of Pakistan and to regulate the terms and conditions of their employment and to lay down rules regarding ancillary matters related thereto. On September 1973, the Act was ratified and on September 29, 1973, the Act was published in the Gazette of Pakistan, Extraordinary, Part I.
The act has four chapters and 26 sections. The first chapter (Introduction) defines the essential terms related to this Act.
In the second chapter, the restrictions and conditions of civil servants are described. Chapter 3 contains miscellaneous provisions while Section 25 of Chapter 4 authorizes the President or a person authorized by him to make such rules as he deems necessary or necessary to carry out the purposes of this Act. Consider it expedient.
4. Civil Servants (Appointment, Promotion, Transfer) Rules, 1973
In exercise of the powers conferred by Section 25 of the Civil Servants Act, 1973, the President framed the Civil Servants (Appointment, Promotion, Transfer) Rules, 1973.
These rules consist of five parts and twenty one chapters. The first part defines the terms used in the rules and specifies the appointing authorities to various posts. The second part provides for appointment by promotion or transfer, the third part for initial appointment, the fourth part for ad hoc appointment and the fifth part for probationary period of appointees.
5. Rules for appointment to ministerial posts
The Personnel Division, in exercise of its powers under these rules, has prescribed the procedure, qualifications and other conditions for appointment to ministerial posts in the Ministries/Divisions and Departments under the Federal Government.
6. Miscellaneous Rules and Regulations for Civil Servants
The following rules and regulations have also been made for civil servants:
(1)	Government Servants (Conduct) Rules, 1964
(2)	Civil Servants (Eligibility and Discipline) Rules, 1973
()	 Salary, allowances and other benefits for civil servants
(4)	Pension and Gratuity Rules for Civil Servants
(5)	 Rules of Leave (Revised), 1980
(6)	 General Provident Fund Rules
(7)	Federal Employees' Provident Fund and Group Insurance Act, 1969
(8)	The Civil Servants (Appeals) Rules, 1977
(9)	 Rules and procedures relating to professional job groups
Offices under the Controller General of Accounts
Chapter 16
Armed forces
1. Command of the Armed Forces
According to Article 243 of the Constitution, the Federal Government shall have the command and control of the armed forces.
2. Power of the President
Without affecting the generality of the foregoing order, the Supreme Command of the Armed Forces shall vest in the President.
The President shall, subject to law, have the power to
(a) establish and maintain the Army, Naval and Air Forces of Pakistan and the reserve forces of those forces;
(b) grant commissions in these forces;
The President, on the advice of the Prime Minister, shall appoint the Chairman, Joint Chiefs of Staff Committee, Chief of Army Staff, Chief of Naval Staff and Chief of Air Staff and shall fix their salaries and allowances.
3. Oath of Armed Forces
Every member of the armed forces shall take oath in the text given in Schedule III of the Constitution.
4. Officials of the Armed Forces
The armed forces shall defend Pakistan against external aggression or threat of war under the direction of the Federal Government and act in aid of civil authorities subject to law, when called upon to do so; However, the validity of any directive issued by the Federal Government shall not be challenged in any court.
Chapter 17
Federal Public Service Commission
Article 242 of the Constitution stipulates that the Majlis Shura (Parliament) may issue laws relating to the affairs of the Federation and the Provincial Assembly of a province may make orders for the establishment and composition of the Public Service Commission through a law relating to the affairs of that province. will
1. Executive office
The officers of the Federal Public Service Commission shall be as follows;
(a) to conduct tests and examinations for the recruitment of such persons other than officers of the Armed Forces of Pakistan who are appointed by the President of the State on the recommendations of the High-powered Selection Board constituted for the purpose in the All Pakistan Jobs, Federation; It is done on fixed posts related to civil services and federal affairs.
(b) To advise the President of the State on the matters of the above jobs and posts on the merits and procedure of recruitment and on any other matter that may be entrusted to the Commission by the President of the State. Recruitment in these orders refers to initial appointment other than promotion or transfer out of the three modes of appointment.
When the President of the State has not accepted the advice of the Commission, he will inform the Commission about it.
2. Annual reports
The Commission shall be required to submit an annual report of its performance to the President and the President shall arrange for a copy of the said report to be submitted to the National Assembly and the Senate.
Chapter 18
Financial Procedures of the Federal Government
1. Federal Consolidated Fund
The Federal Consolidated Fund shall consist of the following sums:
(a)	 All revenues received by the Federal Government
(b) All loans issued by the Federal Government
(c) all sums received in respect of repayment of any loan;
2. Official account of the Federation
The official account of the Federation shall include all other sums which:
(a) received by or on behalf of the Federal Government;
(b) be received by or submitted to the Supreme Court or any other court established under the authority of the Federation.
3. Custody of Federal Consolidated Fund and Government Accounts etc
Custody of the Federal General Fund, payment of funds into this fund, withdrawal of funds from it, payment of funds into the official account of the Federation and withdrawal of funds from it, and all matters related or ancillary to the above-mentioned matters of Majlis Shura (Parliament). shall be governed by the Act
4. Annual Balance Sheet/Budget
The federal government will present the estimated income and expenditure status of the federal government for each fiscal year to the National Assembly. The following amounts shall be shown separately in the annual balance sheet.
(a)	such sums as may be required to meet the expenses which the Constitution has prescribed to be owed to the Federal General Fund; And
(b) such sums as may be required to meet such other expenses as may be proposed to be paid from the Federal General Fund. And a distinction will be kept between the expenses and other expenses from the calculation of the income.
5. Expenditures owed to the Federal General Fund
The following expenditures shall be charges to the Federal General Fund:
(a) allowances payable to the President and other expenses and allowances incidental to his office which shall be payable to the following;
(a)	Judges of the Supreme Court
(b) Chief Election Commissioner
(c) Chairman and Deputy Chairman of the Senate
6. Procedure for Annual Balance Sheet
(1) That portion of the annual balance sheet relating to the expenditure due from the Federal General Fund may be debated in the National Assembly but shall not be submitted to the National Assembly for a vote.
(2) That part of the annual balance sheet which relates to other expenditure shall be presented to the National Assembly in the form of demand money and the Assembly shall be allowed to approve or refuse to approve any demand or specify any demand therein. There will be a power to sanction with the gift of money made
(3) No demand shall be made without the recommendation of the Federal Government.
The Prime Minister will present a table endorsed by his signature in the National Assembly. This table shall specify the following:
(a)	of sums approved or contemplated to be approved by the National Assembly;
(b) such miscellaneous sums as may be required to meet the expenditure due from the Federal Fund but such amount shall not exceed the amount shown in the statement of status previously presented to the National Assembly. This approved table shall be presented to the National Assembly but shall not be debated or voted upon;
(c) No expenditure from the Federal General Fund shall be deemed to have been formally approved unless it has been set forth in an approved schedule and the said schedule has been laid before the National Assembly.
(4) Speaker and Deputy Speaker of the National Assembly
(5) Chief Accountant
(a) Supreme Court, Auditor General (Accountant General) Department, Chief Election Commissioner; and administrative expenses of the Office of the Election Commission, the Senate and the National Assembly, including allowances payable to officers and employees;
(b) all debt obligations payable by the Federal Government, including interest, expenses, deposit payments, repayment of capital or outstanding and acquisition of loans and repayment and disbursement/repayment of loans guaranteed by the Federal General Fund; Other related expenses;
(c) sums required to comply with any judgment, award or arbitration award of any court or tribunal against Pakistan;
(d)	Such other sums as may be aforesaid by the Constitution or by an Act of the Majlis Shura (Parliament) declared to be due.
7. Additional and excess amounts
If in a financial year there is insufficient money for a particular service or if there is a need to spend on a new service or an excess of money has been spent on a service, the federal government has the power to sanction the expenditure from the federal general fund. And submit a supplementary status report or additional status report before the National Assembly.
The rest of the process on these status names will be the same as on the annual balance sheet.
8. Power to sanction expenditure in case of dissolution of National Assembly
According to Article 86, the Federal Government may approve expenditure from the Federal General Fund for any part of a financial year not exceeding four months for the approval of estimated expenditure during the dissolution of the National Assembly.
Chapter 19
Accountant General of Pakistan (Auditor General)
1. Appointment of Auditor General
According to Article 168 of the Constitution, the Auditor General appoints an Accountant General.
Before assuming office, the Auditor General/Accountant General takes oath before the Chief Justice of Pakistan. The text of the oath is listed in the Third Schedule of the Constitution.
2. Duties and Powers
The functions and powers of the Auditor General/Accountant General are as follows:
(a) Calculations
(1)	 Shall be responsible for keeping the accounts of the Federation and the Provinces, except Railways and Defence.
However, the President of the State may by a general or special order direct the Auditor General/Accountant General to keep the accounts of the Federation relating to defense and railways or the accounts of an autonomous body established by the Federation or a province.
(2)	In so far as the accounts of the Federation are concerned, the President of the State and in so far as the accounts of the Provinces are concerned, the Governor may, if he so desires, after consultation with the Auditor General/Accountant General, by rules create scope for the Auditor General/Accountant General to Relinquish the responsibility of preparing the accounts of a particular service or department.
(3)	The President of the State may, if he so desires, after consultation with the Auditor General/Accountant General, make provision by rules to relieve the Auditor General/Accountant General from the responsibility of preparing accounts of a particular grade or nature.
(4)	The Auditor General/Accountant General shall prepare a statement of accounts (including the breakdown of accounts) prepared by him each year from the accounts prepared by him and from the accounts of other persons responsible for keeping official accounts. which shall record the annual receipts and disbursements for the purposes of the Federation and of each Province, fully explained in the respective periods, and shall submit such accounts to the Federal Government, or, as the case may be, to the Provincial Government, on such date as may be which he shall determine with the consent of the Government concerned.
(5)	The Auditor General/Accountant General shall comply with the general or special orders of the President, or as the case may be, the Governor to show any particular matter or matters of a special nature under specified periods in the accounts. However, before issuing such orders as mentioned above, the President or, as the case may be, the Governor shall consult the Auditor General/Accountant General.
(b) General statement of financial position
It shall be the duty of the Auditor General/Accountant General to prepare and submit to the President a general financial position every year in such form as he may decide with the approval of the President. In this general financial statement he shall include a summary of the accounts of the Federation and all the provinces for the previous year and particulars of their arrears and liabilities and shall include all such information as to their financial position. will be done which the President of the State will order to be included in this status report.
(c) Accounting/Audit
It shall be the duty of the Auditor General/Accountant General to:
(1)	He should account for all the expenditure incurred from the federal and provincial funds and ascertain whether the sums shown in the accounts as paid were lawfully available and for the services and purposes for which they were provided. They have been utilized and whether the expenditure is consistent with the authority under which the expenditure is incurred
(2)	To account for all federal and provincial transactions relating to loans, trusts, outstanding funds, advances, pending accounts and remittances.
(3)	Compile the commercial, industrial and profit and loss accounts and personal balances kept under the department of the President of the State or the Governor of a province.
(4)	To account to any authorized body or body established by the Federation or a province and in each case to the President, or as the case may be, to the Governor, report on the expenditure, transactions or accounts accounted for.
The Auditor General/Accountant General shall, with the approval of the President or the Governor, or if he so directs, audit and report on the following:
(a)	 about any department of the federal government or provincial government;
(b) in respect of store accounts maintained in any office or department of the Federal Government or the Provincial Government;
The accounts of the Federation and the Provinces are kept in such form and in accordance with such principles and methods as the Auditor General/Accountant General may prescribe with the approval of the President.
3. Reports of the Auditor General/Accountant General
According to Article 171 of the Constitution, the reports of the Auditor General/Accountant General on the accounts of the Federation are submitted to the President who presents them to the National Assembly.
Reports of the Accountant General relating to a province are submitted to the governor of that province who presents them to the provincial assembly.
Chapter 20
Controller General of Accounts
1. Accountability
According to Articles 168 and 170 of the Constitution, the responsibility of performing the duties of accounting and accounting (auditing) has been given to the Auditor General of Pakistan.
From July 1, 2001, the functions of accounting and bookkeeping were separated and the government decided that the scale of accounts by the President would be the same. An officer of 22 will be appointed as Controller General of Accounts.
2. Duties of Controller General
(1) Shall be responsible for preparing and keeping the accounts of the Federation, Provinces and Districts. These accounts shall be prepared in accordance with the methods and principles laid down by the Auditor General/Accountant General, with the approval of the President, and then these accounts shall be maintained for future reference.
(2) Authorize the Federal and Provincial Governments to pay and withdraw approved budgets from their general fund and public accounts.
(3) The President of the State under the Federal Government or the Provincial Governor may give the responsibility of preparing and maintaining the accounts of any institution or authorized body established under his province.
(4) in consultation with the Ministry of Finance and the Provincial Department of Finance shall lay down rules for the internal financial control of the Government Departments;
(5) advise on accounting procedures for new schemes, programs or activities initiated by the Government concerned;
(6) At the end of each financial year, in accordance with the schedule prescribed by the Auditor-General, he shall submit to the officer appointed by the Auditor-General, the accounts prepared by him or by any other responsible person; showing the annual receipts and disbursements of each province;
(7) shall furnish to the Federal Government, the Provincial Governments and the District Governments such information from the accounts prepared by them as they may require.
(8) establish and properly maintain an effective system of pension, provident fund and retirement benefits in consultation with the Government concerned;
(9) The Accounting/Audit Department shall liaise with the concerned departments for the settlement of accounting/audit observations;
(10) provide facilities for the training of its officers and subordinate staff, formulate curriculum and set training standards;
3. Offices under the Controller General of Accounts
The offices declared by the federal and respective provincial governments and the officers working in those offices, at the federal, provincial and district levels, will work under the Comptroller General.
Currently these offices include the following accounting institutions.
(1)	Governor-General of Pakistan and his subordinate offices;
(2)	 Nazim-Ala Askari and his subordinate offices;
(3)	 Offices of Provincial Governors and their subordinate offices;
(4)	Chief Accounts Officer/Accountant Senior, Departmental Accounts Offices;
(5)	Other departmental accounting institutions and their subordinate offices
The Controller shall be the administrative head of all his subordinate offices and shall have full power of transfer and appointment in his institution.
4. Reports
The Comptroller-General of Accounts shall prepare the prescribed reports for each financial year in accordance with the procedure and the Auditor-General of Pakistan on all such accounts prepared directly by his subordinate offices or by the offices of his subordinate officers or other bodies. These reports include the following:
(1)	Bonding and financial calculations
(2)	 Consolidated and general financial position including summary accounts
(3)	Statements and summaries of monthly and quarterly accounts
