Chapter 1
Units of the Federation of Pakistan
1. Territories of the Federal Republic
The Islamic Republic of Pakistan is a federal state consisting of four federal units and other territories.
Each federal unit is called a province. The details of these four provinces and other areas are as follows:
1. Province of Baluchistan, Province of Punjab, Province of Khyber Pakhtunkhwa and Province of Sindh;
2. Area of Capital Islamabad;
3. Federally Administered Tribal Areas; And
4. Such states and territories to join Pakistan through accession or otherwise.
The Majlis Shura (Parliament) may by law admit new states or territories into the Federation on such terms and conditions as it deems fit.
2. Units of the Federation of Pakistan (Provinces)
-Islamic republic of Pakistan
3. Principal Institutions of the Federation
Like a modern state, the Islamic Republic of Pakistan has three basic institutions of state at the federal level.
(a) Legislature (legislative body): Majlis Shura (Parliament) which consists of the President and two Houses (Senate and National Assembly).
(b) Administration: Federal Government; Administration of Federal Tribal Areas and Administration of the Capital Territory Islamabad
(c) Judiciary: Supreme Court (Supreme Court of Pakistan)
4. Provincial Basic Institutions
(1) Like the three basic institutions of the Federation of Pakistan, according to the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, three basic institutions have also been formed in each province.
(a) Legislature (unicameral legislative body)	: provincial assembly
(b) Administration				: Provincial Govt
(c) Judiciary				 : Supreme Court (High Court)
(2) The constitutional head of each province is the Governor.
The people of each province elect the members of the provincial assembly on the basis of adult voting.
The unicameral provincial assembly is responsible for legislation at the provincial level.
The majority of these elected members choose the Chief Minister.
The Chief Minister is the head of the provincial government, he performs the duties of the chief administrator of the province.
The cabinet consisting of provincial ministers, headed by the Chief Minister, assists and advises the Governor in the discharge of his duties as per the constitutional provisions.
(3) Departments are responsible for carrying out the official functions of the provincial government.
These departments are collectively called Provincial Secretariat.
The Provincial Secretariat is headed by the Chief Secretary.
The Chief Secretary also performs the duties of the Provincial Cabinet Secretary.
He coordinates and supervises the activities of all departments.
(4) Provincial departments are assigned official functions within a clear and specific scope.
This is determined by the Chief Minister.
The Chief Minister gives a department or a part of it or several departments under the custody of a minister.
All official affairs are carried out in accordance with provincial rules and guidelines.
Provincial administrative structure
Chapter 2
Governor: The constitutional head of the province
1. Governor: The representative of the federal government
According to the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, 1973, parliamentary rule has been introduced in the provinces as well as the federation.
Generally, in federal countries, the same kind of system is created in the federal government, the same kind of government structure is created in the federal units.
In Pakistan, the Governor is considered to be the representative of the federal government.
2. Terms of appointment
The President appoints the Governor on the advice of the Prime Minister. The terms of appointment of the Governor are as follows:
(1) That person is eligible to be elected as a member of the National Assembly;
(2) be at least thirty-five (35) years of age;
(iii) be a registered voter;
(4) be a resident of the relevant province;
3. Term of office
The Governor shall hold office until the pleasure of the President. He may resign his office by writing under his signature to the President.
4. Oath of Office
The Governor shall, before assuming office, take an oath before the Chief Justice of the High Court in the text prescribed in the Third Schedule to the Constitution of Pakistan.
5. Terms of office
The terms of office of the Governor are as follows:
(a) The Governor shall not accept any position of profit or any other position in the service of Pakistan which carries a right to remuneration as a reward for rendering services.
(b) The Governor shall not be a candidate for election as a member of Majlis Shura (Parliament) or any Provincial Assembly.
(c) If a member of the Majlis Shura (Parliament) or a Provincial Assembly is appointed as the Governor, his seat in the Majlis Shura (Parliament) or the Provincial Assembly shall become vacant on the day on which he assumes office.
6. Acting Governor
When the Governor is unable to perform his duties due to absence in Pakistan or for any other reason, the Speaker of the Provincial Assembly shall perform the duties of the Governor in the absence of the Governor until the Governor returns to Pakistan or until he assumes his duties for any other reason. In the absence of the Speaker, a person nominated by the President shall perform the duties of the Governor.
7. The Governor will act on the advice of the Cabinet or the Chief Minister
In the performance of his duties under the Constitution, the Governor shall act in accordance with the advice of the Cabinet or the Chief Minister. However, within 15 days the Governor may order the Cabinet or the Chief Minister to reconsider the said advice. After reconsideration by the Cabinet or the Chief Minister, the Governor shall act within ten days as per the advice given.
8. Dissolution of Provincial Assembly
(1) According to Article 112 of the Constitution, if the Chief Minister advises, the Governor will dissolve the Provincial Assembly.
Otherwise, the Provincial Assembly shall be dissolved at the end of forty-eight hours after such advice is given by the Chief Minister.
Chief Minister does not mean a Chief Minister against whom a no-confidence resolution has been notified in the Provincial Assembly but has not been voted on, or against whom a no-confidence resolution has been passed.
(2) The Governor can also dissolve the Provincial Assembly at his discretion but with the prior approval of the President. The Governor will exercise this discretionary right in such a case that a vote of no confidence has been passed against the Chief Minister and no other member of the Provincial Assembly has the confidence of the majority of the members of the Provincial Assembly as per the Constitution and this situation is for this purpose. It was known in the convened meeting of the Provincial Assembly.
(3) When the Provincial Assembly is dissolved before the end of its term, within ninety days from the date of dissolution, it shall fix a date for holding general elections to the Assembly.
9. Supervisory Cabinet
(1) On the completion of his term or on his dissolution under Article 112 of the Constitution, the Governor of the Province shall, under Article 224 of the Constitution, appoint a Caretaker Cabinet.
(2) The detailed procedure for the appointment of caretaker chief minister and caretaker cabinet is described in Chapter No. 24.
10. Address to the Provincial Assembly
The Governor can address the Provincial Assembly and order the attendance of the members for this purpose.
11. Governor's assent to draft law (Bill).
When the Provincial Assembly passes a bill, it shall be submitted to the governor for assent. The governor shall assent the bill within ten days, or in the case of a bill that is not a finance bill, with a written message to the bill. shall return to the Provincial Assembly to reconsider the Bill or any part thereof and to consider any amendment specified in the message.
The returned bill shall be reconsidered by the Provincial Assembly and if the Provincial Assembly passes the bill again, with or without amendment, by a majority vote of the members present, it shall again be submitted to the Governor and the Governor shall within ten days Will ratify the bill. If the Governor does not do so within the prescribed period, it shall be deemed ratified.
After the assent of the Governor, the Bill shall become a Bill and shall be called an Act of the Provincial Assembly.
12. Duties of the Chief Minister in relation to the Governor
(1) Shall keep the Governor informed of all matters relating to provincial administration and of all proposals for legislation under Article 131 of the Constitution which the Provincial Government intends to bring before the Provincial Assembly.
(2) He shall inform the Governor of the decisions of the Cabinet relating to the administration of the Province and proposed legislation.
(3) submit for reconsideration to the Cabinet such matter as the Governor may direct for reconsideration in accordance with Article 105 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan.
Chapter 3
provincial assembly
1. Formation of Provincial Assembly
A unicameral provincial assembly has been constituted for each province.
The number of members of this provincial assembly has been determined in proportion to the population of each province.
The Provincial Assembly consists of general seats, reserved seats for women and non-Muslims as detailed below:
2. The right to vote
Any such person shall have the right to vote; If
(a) he is a citizen of Pakistan;
(b) he is not less than eighteen years of age;
(c) his name is entered in the electoral roll of a constituency in the province concerned;
(d) He has not been declared of insanity by a competent court.
3. Constituencies
For the election of a Provincial Assembly
(a) The constituencies for ordinary provincial seats shall be single-member regional constituencies and the members to fill the said seats shall be elected by direct and free vote.
(2) Each respective province shall be a single constituency for all seats reserved for women and non-Muslims in the provinces.
(3) to fill the reserved seats for women and non-Muslims assigned to a province, from the list of candidates of political parties, by proportional representation, of the general seats obtained by each political party in the provincial assembly. will be selected based on the total number of The total number of ordinary seats won by a political party shall include those successful independent candidates who formally join said political party within three days of the publication of the names of the successful candidates in the official gazette.
4. Term of Provincial Assembly
Provincial Assembly shall, unless prematurely dissolved, continue for a term of five years from the date of its first meeting and shall be dissolved at the end of its term.
5. Election of Speaker and Deputy Speaker
A Provincial Assembly shall, in its first session after a general election, elect a Speaker and a Deputy Speaker from among its members.
6. Summoning and dismissing the meeting of the Provincial Assembly
Governor from time to time
(a) The meeting of the Provincial Assembly may be convened at such time and place as it thinks fit.
(b) Can dismiss the meeting of the Provincial Assembly.
7. Dissolution of Provincial Assembly
(1) According to Article 112 of the Constitution, the Governor shall dissolve the Provincial Assembly. If the Chief Minister so advises him and the Provincial Assembly, unless previously dissolved, shall be dissolved at the expiration of forty-eight hours after such advice has been given by the Chief Minister. against whom notice of a resolution of no-confidence vote has been given in the Provincial Assembly but no vote has been taken on it or against whom a resolution of no-confidence vote has been passed.
(2) The Governor may also dissolve the Provincial Assembly at his discretion, but subject to the prior approval of the President, while after a vote of no confidence is passed against the Chief Minister, any other member of the Provincial Assembly shall have the confidence of the majority of the members in the meeting of the Provincial Assembly. do not keep
Chapter 4
Provincial government and constitutional authority of the province
1. Chief Minister
The meeting of the provincial assembly will be held on the 21st day after the general election of the assembly, but the governor can call the meeting before that.
After the election of the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker, the Provincial Assembly shall, without any further action, elect a Chief Minister from among its members who shall be elected by a majority vote of the total membership of the Provincial Assembly.
The Governor shall ask the elected member to assume the office of Chief Minister and before assuming office he shall take oath before the Governor in the form given in Schedule III of the Constitution.
2. Number of terms for office
There will be no restriction on the number of terms for the post of Chief Minister.
The Chief Minister shall hold office during the pleasure of the Governor.
If the governor is satisfied that the chief minister is not getting the confidence of the majority of the members of the provincial assembly, he will call a meeting of the provincial assembly and order the chief minister to get a vote of confidence from the assembly.
3. Resignation of the Chief Minister
The Chief Minister can resign from his office by writing under his signature to the Governor.
4. Continuity of Chief Minister in office
The Governor can ask the Chief Minister to remain in office until his successor takes over as Chief Minister.
5. A vote of no confidence against the Chief Minister
The resolution of vote of no confidence against the Chief Minister, which is presented by at least twenty percent of the total number of the Provincial Assembly, can be passed by the Provincial Assembly.
No vote shall be taken before the expiry of the period of thirty days from the day on which this resolution is presented in the Assembly or after the period of seven days.
If this resolution is approved by the majority of the members of the Provincial Assembly, then the Chief Minister will not hold the post.
6. Cabinet
There will be a Cabinet of Ministers headed by the Chief Minister. The Cabinet shall assist and advise the Governor in the discharge of his duties.
7. Number of cabinet members
The total strength of the Cabinet shall not exceed fifteen members or eleven percent of the total membership of a Provincial Assembly, whichever is greater.
8. Overall responsibility of the cabinet
The Cabinet as a whole will be accountable to the Provincial Assembly.
9. Provincial Ministers
(1) The Governor shall appoint the Provincial Ministers from among the members of the Provincial Assembly on the advice of the Chief Minister. Before assuming office, a provincial minister shall take an oath before the Governor in the text given in Schedule III of the Constitution. A provincial minister may resign from his office by writing to the governor under his signature or the governor may dismiss him from office on the advice of the chief minister.
(2) A Minister who has not been a member of the Provincial Assembly for a continuous period of six months shall cease to be a Minister at the end of the said period and shall not be re-appointed as a Minister before the dissolution of the said Assembly unless he is a member of that Assembly. not be elected as a member of This condition does not mean that the Chief Minister or any other Minister shall not have the right to continue in office during any such period when the Provincial Assembly is dissolved nor to appoint any person as Chief Minister or Minister during any such period. will be prohibited.
10. Advisors and Special Assistants
There will be advisers and special assistants to the Chief Minister, who will be appointed by the Chief Minister. The duties of these advisers and special assistants shall be determined from time to time.
11. Duties of Parliamentary Secretary
(1) Subject to any general or special order issued by the Chief Minister, the Parliamentary Secretary of a Department shall perform such parliamentary functions or related duties relating to the Department as may be assigned to him by the Minister in charge of the Department.
(2) A Parliamentary Secretary shall not undertake any work which interferes with the internal working or management of his department, his affiliated department or regional office.
12. Advocate General
(1) The Advocate General is the highest law officer of the province.
(2) The Governor of each province shall appoint a person who is qualified to be a judge of a High Court as Advocate General of the province.
(3) It shall be the duty of the Advocate General to advise the Provincial Government on such legal matters and to perform such other duties of a legal nature as may be referred or assigned to him by the Provincial Government.
(4) The Advocate General shall hold office during the pleasure of the Governor and shall not engage in private practice while holding such office.
(5) The Advocate General may resign from his office by writing under his signature to the Governor.
13. Administrative authority of the province
(1) According to Article 137 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, the administrative authority of the province shall apply to those matters about which the provincial assembly has the power to make laws.
(2) In any matter in respect of which both the Majlis Shura (Parliament) and the Provincial Assembly of a province have the power to make laws, the administrative power of the province shall be subject to and limited by the administrative power conferred by the Constitution or the Majlis Shura (Parliament). has been expressly delegated to the Federal Government or its authorized body by a law made by
14. Assignment of duties to subordinates
On the recommendation of the Provincial Government, the Provincial Assembly may, by any law, delegate its duties to officers or bodies under the Provincial Government.
15. Use of administrative authority
The administrative authority of the province will be exercised by the provincial government consisting of the chief minister and the provincial ministers in the name of the governor.
The provincial government will perform its duties through the Chief Minister.
The Chief Minister shall act directly or through the Provincial Ministers to carry out his duties.
Chapter 5
Conduct of official affairs in the province
1. Execution of administrative actions in the name of the Governor
(1) According to Article 139 of the Constitution, all administrative actions of the provincial government shall be done in the name of the Governor.
(2) The Provincial Government shall by rules specify the manner in which orders issued in the name of the Governor and other documents executed shall be authenticated.
And the validity of any order or document so authenticated shall not be challenged in any Court on the ground that it was not framed or completed by the Governor.
(3) The Constitution has empowered each provincial government to make rules for the determination and performance of its functions.
2. Rulers
(1) In exercise of the powers conferred by Article 139 of the Constitution, each provincial government has formulated rules.
These rules include the formation and organization of departments at the provincial level and their list, distribution between departments, guidelines for carrying out the work of the provincial government, consultation between provincial departments, the procedure for approaching the Chief Minister and the Governor, Legislative procedure and relations with the Provincial Assembly etc. are included.
(2) Under the Rules, the Chief Minister shall coordinate all policy matters in the Provincial Government and no policy decision shall be taken without the approval of the Chief Minister. The policy decision taken by the Chief Minister shall neither be changed nor violated without consulting the Chief Minister. It will be the duty of the Minister to assist the Chief Minister in formulating the policy. He shall be responsible for the policy relating to his department and shall inform the Chief Minister of any important matter which he has dealt with without consulting the Chief Minister.
3. Instructions Trustee/Instructions Secretariat
Under the rules of each province, the concerned department has issued detailed instructions for the performance of official work in the provincial secretariat.
In these instructions, the duties and responsibilities of various government officials have been described.
Detailed instructions are given about the steps a case goes through in a government department from initiation to final decision. Registering and initiating proceedings on receipt of mail in the departments, opening files on various subjects, recording the status of files, submitting files to higher officials for decision, issuing orders after decision, issuing files. To take care of and take appropriate measures for their protection, all these matters and other related matters are described in detail in the instructions trust.
4. Verbal orders
(1) All orders issued by the Provincial Government shall be in writing.
In case of verbal orders, the recipient shall put the said orders in writing and as soon as possible, the issuing authority shall submit the orders for verification of the orders.
(2) If any order issued is against the law, rules and regulations or government policy, it shall be the responsibility of the next subordinate officer to point out the same to the authority issuing the order.
If the aforesaid superior does not agree, he shall refer the matter to the superior superior for appropriate decision.
5. Orders and documents, agreements and contracts
(1) Except in cases where an officer is specially authorized by the Chief Minister to sign any order or document on behalf of the Government, on every order or document the Secretary, Special Secretary, Additional Secretary, Deputy Secretary, Section The officer, officer-in-charge or any other officer duly notified by the department concerned shall sign and such signature shall be deemed to be a valid attestation of the said order or document.
(2) The Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs is empowered to issue directions for the preparation and execution of contracts and assurances of property.
Chapter 6
Provincial Secretariat and other provincial offices
1. Provincial Secretariat
(1) Departments are assigned the primary responsibility for carrying out government affairs at the provincial level.
These departments are collectively called Provincial Secretariat.
The Provincial Secretariat consists of the departments listed in the second column of Schedule I of the Provincial Rules.
(2) The Provincial Secretariat is headed by the Chief Secretary.
2. Chief Secretary
The duties of the Chief Secretary are as follows:
(a) perform the duties of Secretary to the Provincial Cabinet;
(b) is generally responsible for all matters affecting public order;
(c) coordinates and supervises the activities of all departments;
(d) has the power to request any matter or information from any department, affiliated department, regional office or district government;
(h) All matters referred to the Chief Minister by the Departments are returned by the Chief Secretary.
3. Dept
'Department' means a comprehensive and complete administrative unit of the Provincial Secretariat responsible for carrying out the work of the Provincial Government within a clear and specific scope.
'proclamation' is formally issued by the provincial government to grant the status of a department to an administrative unit.
And it is registered in Schedule I of Provincial Rules. For example, Finance Department, Health Department, Food Department etc
(2) The Chief Minister may create new departments, reconstitute existing departments and reduce or increase their number.
(3) Affiliated departments and autonomous bodies are not part of the Provincial Secretariat.
4. Affiliated Deptt
Adjunct departments of each department are established as necessary to provide expert advice on technical aspects of policy issues and to implement the policy formulated by the government.
These subsidiary departments work directly under their respective departments.
The attached department is mentioned in the first schedule of the rules of each province. For example, the attached department of the Home Department is: Nizamat Civil Defense and the attached department of the Health Department is: Nizamat Khittam Sehat.
5. Autonomous body
An entity established by an Act of the Provincial Assembly or as a Public Limited Company or under the Trust Act which carries out various types of activities.
In Schedule A I of the Rules of the Government of Punjab, autonomous bodies of various departments have been mentioned.
For example, University of Agriculture Faisalabad, Punjab Agricultural Research Board, Institute of Development Lahore etc.
6. Company
In the public sector, a company formed by the Government of Punjab which is mentioned in Schedule A of the Rules of the Government of Punjab, eg Lahore Transport Company under the Department of Transport, Department of Housing, Urban Development and Public Health; Punjab Land Development Company etc. under Engineering.
7. Regional Office
Regional office means an office declared by the Punjab Government.
8. Special Institution
Such institution of the province of Punjab which is mentioned in Schedule I of the Rules of the Government of Punjab, 2011;
For example, a special institution of the Finance Department of the Government of Punjab: Punjab Pension Fund Bank; Department of Higher Education Special Institution: Aitchison College, Lahore; A special agency of the Department of Industry, Trade and Investment of the Government of Punjab:
Institute of Technical Education and Vocational Training (TIOTA)
Chapter 7
Allocation of official work between departments
1. Determination of official work
(1) It is the responsibility of the departments to carry out government affairs at the provincial level.
A clear and specific scope of official work has been defined for each department
Schedule II of the Provincial Rules details the work assigned to each department separately.
(2) The Chief Minister has the authority to entrust any subject or matter specified to a department in the Second Schedule of the Rules to any other department.
(3) The Chief Minister may place a department, a part of a department, parts of different departments or more than one department under the custody of a minister.
(4) Any department or any part of a department not entrusted to a Minister shall be in the custody of the Chief Minister.
2. Delegation of authority to District Government
The Chief Minister of Punjab may delegate any function, subject or matter, in whole or in part, to a District Government so that the offices of the District Government established under the Punjab Local Government Ordinance, 2001 (13 of 2001) may perform such functions. .
3. Discrepancy in determination
If there is any doubt as to which department a matter properly belongs to, the matter shall be referred to the Chief Secretary.
If necessary, the Chief Secretary shall obtain the orders of the Chief Minister and the orders so issued shall be final.
4. Department of Services and General Management
(1) To illustrate the work assigned to the departments, the example of the Department of Services and General Management is given. In Punjab province and Sindh province it is called Service and General Management Department while in Khyber Pakhtunkhwa province its name is Personnel and Management Department.
The following government affairs have been assigned to this department:
(a) Personnel Matters: Regulation of all such matters of Provincial Government employees applicable to civil posts related to Provincial affairs.
It serves as the primary office for departmental affairs staff.
In these cases, the recruitment of employees, terms and conditions of employment, conduct and discipline, legal rights and privileges of civil servants, the number and terms and conditions of the personal staff of provincial ministers and provincial employees for appointment on loan to the federal government. Includes selection.
It is also the responsibility of this department to take action on the submissions of the members of Total Pakistan Jobs to the Federal Government.
(b) Chief Minister's Secretariat: This department works as the Secretariat of the Provincial Chief Minister under the leadership of the Provincial Chief Secretary.
All matters referred to the Chief Minister go back to the departments through the Chief Secretary.
(c) Cabinet Secretariat: This department functions as the Secretariat of the Provincial Cabinet.
The Chief Secretary performs the duties of the Cabinet Secretary. The procedure for presentation of matters in the Cabinet is described in Chapter No. 12.
(2) Without the consent of the Department of Services and General Management, no department shall be permitted to issue any orders regarding the following matters:
(a) the reduction or extension of the duties of a department or the transfer of duties from one department to another as specified in the Second Schedule to the Rules;
(b) reorganization or change in status of a department, affiliated department and regional office under the department;
(c) any change in the terms and conditions of employment or statutory rights and privileges of Government servants;
(3) No orders regarding the promotion, promotion or conditions of service of any officer employed in the Finance Department shall be issued or any proposal for the expenditure of the Finance Department shall be approved without the prior consent of this Department.
In these matters, the Chief Secretary will perform the duties of the Finance Secretary.
Chapter No. 8
Internal organization of provincial departments
1. General Instructions
Each Department shall consist of its own Minister, Secretary and such other officers as may be determined by the Government.
A single person can be a minister or secretary of more than one department.
2. Official Head
The official head of the department is the Secretary. A single person can be in charge of more than one department.
3. Head Offices
(1) Each department is divided into sub-departments. Each wing consists of sections/sections and branches.
Each wing is usually headed by an additional secretary.
(2) There shall be one or more Deputy Secretaries working under each Additional Secretary.
A number of section officers work under each Deputy Secretary.
(3) Section officers in a province sometimes work directly under the Additional Secretary.
4. Phrases
Section (Saiga) is the basic administrative unit of every department headed by an officer Saiga (Section Officer).
5. Branch
is the primary unit of the department which functions under the supervision of the Superintendent. The in-charge of the branch is the Section Officer.
Sometimes the Deputy Secretary is directly in charge of the Sections/Branch. A branch is usually an informal organizational unit; For example, Receipt and Issue Branch, Accounts Branch.
6. Organization chart
The organizational chart to explain the internal organization of the departments is given below:
Chapter 9
Distribution of official work among different officers of the department
1. Duties of the Minister
(1) The duties of the Provincial Minister are as follows:
(a) be responsible for policy matters and the performance of the work assigned to the Department;
(b) shall submit matters to the Chief Minister under the Rules;
(c) keep the Chief Minister informed of such important matters as he may deal with without presenting them to the Chief Minister;
(d) conduct the affairs of the Assembly relating to his department.
(2) It is the responsibility of the Minister to consult the Chief Minister in important political, economic and administrative matters related to his department.
2. Responsibilities of the Secretary
(1) The duties of the Secretary shall be as follows:
(a) The Secretary, being the Head of the Department, shall be responsible for the effective management of his Department.
(b) The Secretary shall be responsible for the official matters assigned to the Department under the Rules and for the observance of the rules and regulations, including rules, in the execution of those matters.
(2) It shall be the responsibility of the Secretary, under general or special orders of the Government:
(a) delegate powers to his subordinate officers and in so doing determine the maximum extent of those powers and specify the nature of the matters; Issue clear standing orders based on these powers and lay down procedures for dealing with matters in the department.
(b) issue special orders and instructions to its officers for the performance of the work assigned to the District Government.
3. Secretary and Ministerial Liaison
(1) The Secretary is responsible to the Minister for official matters assigned to the Department.
The Secretary has a responsibility to keep the Minister informed of the performance of the Department and of important matters which have been dealt with without being brought to the attention of the Minister;
(2) The Secretary shall assist the Minister in policy making; and shall inform the Minister of such matters as may be required to be referred to the Chief Minister;
(3) The Secretary shall, with the approval of the Minister, make proposals for legislation to the Cabinet.
(4) The Secretary shall keep the Chief Secretary informed about important matters being dealt with in the Department.
4. Presenting matters to Minister-in-Charge
In presenting a matter for orders to the Minister, the Secretary shall prescribe a prescribed course of action.
5. Procedure in case of disagreement between Secretary and Minister
(1) If the Minister's orders are contrary to any law, regulation or government policy, the Secretary shall refer the matter to the Minister again and draw the Minister's attention to the relevant law, regulation or government policy.
(2) If the Minister does not agree with the Secretary, the Secretary may approach the Chief Minister for orders on the said matter.
6. Implementation of approved policy
The Secretary shall be responsible for the implementation of the approved policy.
7. Additional Secretary
The Additional Secretary is in charge of the Department/Wing and the Secretary as Head determines his duties through Standing Orders.
8. Deputy Secretary
The Secretary determines the duties of the Deputy Secretary by Standing Orders. Several sections work under it.
The Deputy Secretary deals with all matters which do not involve a major policy issue or which he is empowered to deal with under the rules and standing orders.
9. Section Officer
The in-charge of the section is the Section Officer (Afsir Saigha).
Generally, in the provinces, the Prosecution Officer (Afsarasigha) deals with all such cases where there are clear precedents and there is no problem of deviation from these precedents or he is authorized to deal with these cases under the rules and standing orders.
Chapter 10
Inter-departmental consultation
1. General Instructions
(1) When the subject matter of a matter is related to more than one department, the department-in-charge shall be responsible for consultation with the other concerned department. All concerned departments will consider the matter before issuing any order or before presenting any matter to the Chief Minister or the Cabinet.
Urgent cases may, with the approval of the Chief Minister, be exempted from this rule but thereafter the matter shall be brought to the notice of the concerned departments as soon as possible.
(2) In case of disagreement between departments, the Minister primarily concerned shall refer the matter to the Chief Minister; However, in case of an urgent matter, basically the minister concerned can present the matter to the Chief Minister at any stage.
2. INSTRUCTIONS FOR CONSULTATION OF SPECIFIC DEPARTMENTS
Detailed instructions have been issued in the Rules for consultation with the following departments:
(1) Department of Services and General Management (Baluchistan Province, Punjab Province, Sindh Province) / Personnel and Management Department (Kyber Pakhtunkhwa Province)
(2) Department of Finance
(3) Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs
(4) Interior Department (Sindh Province, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa Province)
3. Department of Services and General Management
(1) The Department of Services and General Management shall be responsible for the following matters:
0 shall prescribe the basic principles of rules and regulations for public servants, including the recruitment, conditions of employment and discipline of public servants;
0 will co-ordinate employment policy under all departments, for the purpose of harmonizing the terms and conditions of employment of Government servants;
shall enjoy the rights and privileges granted to public servants under any law;
0. Shall determine the number and terms of employment of the Minister's personal staff.
0 To deal with the petitions written by the members of "Total Pakistan Jobs" to the Federal Government;
0 To elect officers for appointment under the Federal Government, except for the post of Secretary and above;
0 To act as Secretariat to the Chief Minister and the Provincial Cabinet;
0 To take action on matters related to the Council of Common Interests and inter-provincial coordination.
(2) No department shall, without the consent of the Department of Services and General Administration, pass such orders other than orders issued under the general or special powers conferred on the Department of Services and General Administration in respect of the following matters: :
(a) reducing or extending the scope of the functions of any department specified in the Second Schedule or transferring such functions from one department to another;
(b) reorganization or change in status of commands, attached departments and regional offices directly under the control of a department;
(c) interpretation of rules and orders relating to employment matters other than rules and orders issued by the Finance Department;
(d) changes in terms and conditions or constitutional rights and privileges of public servants;
(3) No orders shall be issued and no proposal of expenditure shall be approved regarding the promotion, promotion or terms and conditions of employment of any officer employed in the Finance Department without the prior consent of the Department of Services and General Management.
In these matters, the Chief Secretary will act as the Secretary of the Finance Department.
4. Consultation with Finance Department
(1) No department shall, without prior consultation with the Finance Department, be empowered to issue any orders, except such orders as may be issued by the Finance Department under general or special delegated powers, which directly or indirectly affecting the finances of the Province or relating in particular to the following:
(a) the relinquishment, waiver or assignment of, or guarantee of, actual or potential benefits; Leasing of land, minerals, forests or hydropower;
(b) expenses for which there is no provision in the budget;
(c) change in the number or name of the basic scale of pay of a post or in the terms and conditions of Government servants or in their constitutional rights and privileges which have financial implications;
(d) levying taxes, duties, fees and cesses (local revenue);
Issuance of loans
0 Amounts reclassified within the budget;
0 Change in financial methods, calculations or budget estimates;
0 Interpretation of rules framed by the Department of Finance;
(2) The Department of Finance shall not make any amendment or interpretation of the Civil Service Rules, which does not have financial implications, without the prior consent of the Department of Services and General Management;
(3) No proposal shall be processed which requires prior consultation of the Finance Department under the rules and the Finance Department has not agreed to the proposal.
Even if the Cabinet decides on this, formal orders on the proposal will be issued only after the Finance Department completes its scrutiny of the details of the proposal.
(4) Except in such cases where powers have been delegated to departments under rules framed by the Finance Department,
Every order of the Administrative Department, authorizing the department to carry out audit, shall be forwarded to the audit authorities by the Finance Department.
5. Consultation with the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs
(1) The Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs shall be consulted in the following matters:
0 Matters relating to substantive legislation;
0 on matters relating to delegated legislation; eg rules and regulations, by-laws/agreements, memoranda of understanding;
Interpretation of original or delegated legislation;
0 on all legal questions arising on a matter;
0 before commencing any civil action against the Government in any court of law;
0 When a civil action is brought against the Government;
(2) for any proposed legislation, original or delegated, the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs shall be consulted;
(3) The Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs is not responsible for initiating legislation, original or delegated. The proper duty of this department is to give proper legal shape to the proposed legislation.
(4) amendment of original laws, legislation to consolidate existing laws or legislation of a merely formal nature; For example, the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs can initiate the repeal or amendment of bills and short title bills.
However, the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs will consult with the concerned department. The department concerned will consider the effect of the proposed law on administration, obtain necessary information, consult and then give its opinion to the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs.
6. Consultation with the Advocate General
(1) The department desirous of consulting the Advocate General shall prepare such clear points on the relevant subject on which the opinion of the Advocate General is required. The Department will forward a complete letter to the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs for consultation with the Advocate General.
However, in matters of urgent nature or if public interest so requires, the department concerned shall, after recording the reasons of urgency, in writing, direct the said points of clarification to the Advocate General for legal opinion.
(2) In cases in which the concerned department wishes to consult the Advocate General through the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs, the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs shall record its comprehensive opinion on the aforementioned legal points and then submit its opinion to the Advocate General. He will send the matter for writing.
(3) If there is a difference of opinion between the Advocate General and the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs, the verbatim opinion of both shall be sent to the concerned department. If the concerned department does not accept the opinion of the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs, the matter will be presented to the Minister of Law and Parliamentary Affairs for decision in the cabinet.
(4) For representation in a matter before the High Court, the Federal Shariat Court and the Supreme Court, with the prior permission of the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs and the approval of the Advocate General, a department shall engage the services of a private legal adviser.
7. Committee of Secretaries
(1) There shall be a Committee of Secretaries to consider matters referred by a Department, Minister or Chief Minister so as to benefit from the experience and collective wisdom of senior officers on the subject under consideration.
(2) If a Secretary desires that a particular matter be considered by the Committee of Secretaries, he shall inform the Department of Services and General Administration of his intention and send a short note to the said Department. This note will form the basis of discussion in the committee meeting.
(3) Well before the meeting of the Department of Services and General Management Committee,
He will inform about the holding of the meeting and will also send the draft (agenda) of the meeting. However, important matters can also be considered by calling a meeting through short notice.
(4) All Secretaries shall attend the meeting of the Committee of Secretaries.
(5) Except in such cases, where it is not considered necessary to write the minutes, the minutes of the meeting of the committee shall be sealed and after the approval of the Chief Minister, it shall be sent to the concerned participants of the meeting.
(6) According to the rules, the department concerned shall take necessary action on the recommendations of the Committee of Secretaries.
Chapter 11
Matters and procedures to be submitted to the Chief Minister
1. Matters to be presented
No order shall be issued without the approval of the Chief Minister in the following cases:
(1) a matter which requires a policy decision; a matter which deviates from a policy decision;
(Note: Deviation from policy decision includes previous decision of Cabinet or Chief Minister.)
(2) the matters mentioned in the relevant schedule of the Provincial Rules;
(3) The Chief Minister may, generally or specifically, order that any matter be referred to him;
(4) The Chief Minister may request any matter or information from any department, affiliated department, regional office or district government.
2. Procedure for presentation of cases
The procedure for submitting matters to the Chief Minister is as follows:
(1) The case submitted to the Chief Minister for orders shall consist of a full, comprehensive and objective summary containing the relevant facts, points for decision and special recommendations of the Minister-in-Charge and where appropriate, a draft of the letter shall be sent with the summary. will
(2) Matters referred to the Chief Minister shall be returned through the Chief Secretary.
3. Matters for information
The matters mentioned in the relevant schedule of the provincial rules will be submitted to the Chief Minister for information.
4. Department of Services and General Management
Department of Services and General Management (Baluchistan Province, Punjab Province, Sindh Province) / Department of Personnel and Management (Kyber Pakhtunkhwa Province) will act as the Secretariat of the Chief Minister and Provincial Cabinet. The Secretariat will be headed by the Chief Secretary.
Chapter 12
Cabinet and its workings
1. Cabinet
(1) The Chief Minister shall be the head of the Cabinet. The Cabinet shall assist and advise the Governor in the discharge of his duties.
(2) The Chief Secretary shall be the Secretary to the Cabinet.
(3) Department of Services and General Administration (Balochistan Province, Punjab Province, Sindh Province) / Department of Personnel and Administration (Kyber Pakhtunkhwa Province) will act as the Secretariat of the Cabinet.
(4) The Cabinet shall collectively be accountable to the Provincial Assembly.
2. Matters to be presented to the Cabinet
(1) official or unofficial proposals for legislation, including draft laws;
(2) Promulgation and repeal of emergency laws;
(3) Budget situation and proposals before presenting the annual budget and other financial statements;
(4) Proposals to impose new taxes;
(5) matters relating to important political, economic and administrative policies;
(6) matters which the Minister-in-Charge considers important enough to be referred to the Cabinet;
(7) important reports and documents to be submitted to the Assembly;
(8) other matters which may be required to be referred to the Cabinet under the Rules;
(9) any matter in respect of which the Chief Minister may wish to be placed before the Cabinet;
(10) As per Article 105 of the Constitution, such matters as require reconsideration at the discretion of the Governor.
3. Authority of Chief Minister
The Chief Minister has the power to direct the procedure for dealing with a matter without presenting it to the Cabinet, in urgent cases or in other exceptional circumstances.
The Cabinet shall be informed, as soon as possible, of such matters dealt with.
4. Method of dealing with Cabinet matters
Matters entrusted to the Cabinet shall be dealt with in the following manner:
(a) by discussion in a Cabinet meeting;
(b) by rotation among Ministers;
(c) by discussion in a Cabinet Committee meeting;
However, the decisions of the Committee shall be ratified by the Cabinet unless otherwise authorized by the Cabinet.
5. Cabinet Committees
The Cabinet may constitute its own Standing or Special Committees and may assign to each Committee a class of matters or a special matter.
6. Procedure for presentation of materials in the cabinet
(1) To present a matter to the Cabinet, the Secretary of the Department concerned shall make a concise and clear summary to the Cabinet,
In which the background of the case and relevant facts, points for decision and recommendations of the minister-in-charge are given, will be sent to the Chief Secretary. The abstract shall be complete in all respects.
Documents necessary for proper understanding of the matter may be attached as annexures.
(2) For the approval in principle of proposed legislation by the Cabinet or for the approval of a draft law or ordinance, the summary to the Cabinet shall state the salient features of such legislation.
(3) If the matter concerns more than one Department, the summary shall not be submitted to the Cabinet until all the Departments concerned have considered it. In case of disagreement, the points of disagreement between these departments will be clearly stated in the abstract.
A copy of the abstract shall be sent by the presenting department to each concerned department along with the submission of the abstract to the Cabinet.
(4) If any proposal contained in the summary to the Cabinet has financial implications, the said summary shall not be submitted to the Cabinet without the consultation and opinion of the Finance Department being included in the summary.
(5) All draft laws, emergency laws or orders having legal effect shall be submitted to the Cabinet after being examined by the Department of Law and Parliamentary Affairs and without any changes made without the knowledge of that Department. will go
(6) No matter shall be accepted for inclusion in the agenda of a meeting of the Cabinet unless it is received by the Chief Secretary at least four full days before the meeting, but if the matter is of an urgent nature, the concerned Secretary shall I may request the Chief Secretary for involvement in this matter.
If the Chief Secretary agrees to the proposal, a note will be sent to the Cabinet for circulation and reasons for its timely submission.
(7) The Department of Services and General Management shall satisfy itself that the documents submitted by the concerned department are complete and proper in all respects.
If the case does not meet the requirements of the relevant rules or guidelines, the case will normally be returned.
Chapter 13
Matters to be submitted to the Governor
1. Orders of the Governor on the advice of the Chief Minister
(1) No order shall be issued without the approval of the Governor on the matters mentioned in the relevant Schedule to the Rules. In order to obtain the approval of the Governor on any of these matters, the department concerned shall include a paragraph in the summary entitled ``Summary for the Chief Minister''. The Chief Minister, with due advice, shall refer the matter to the Governor. The summary will be returned to the Chief Minister after the orders of the Governor.
2. Matters for information
Matters listed in the relevant schedule of the rules will be submitted to the Governor for information through the Chief Minister.
Chapter 14
Provincial Jobs
1. Protection against discrimination in employment
Article 27 of the Constitution declares as follows:
(a) no discrimination shall be made in respect of any appointment to any citizen eligible for appointment in the service of Pakistan solely on the ground of race, religion, caste, sex, residence or place of birth;
(b) Posts may be reserved for the people of a class or region for a maximum period of forty years from the date of coming into force of the Constitution so that they may be adequately represented in the employment of Pakistan. The under-representation of a section or region in the employment of Pakistan should be redressed in such a manner as Majlis Shura.
(c) If certain positions or jobs require the performance of duties and functions which cannot be adequately performed by persons of the other sex, in the interest of the said employment, such positions or jobs shall be reserved for persons of one sex. Can be saved.
(d) any matter in the aforesaid protection to the Government of a province or any of its institutions before appointing a candidate to any of his posts or employment;
Therefore, there will be no objection in imposing the condition of residence of maximum three years in this province.
2. Provincial Public Service Commission
(1) In terms of Article 242 of the Constitution, the Assembly of a province may, by law, make rules for the establishment and constitution of a Public Service Commission relating to the affairs of that province.
(2) The Chairman of the Provincial Public Service Commission constituted for the affairs of a province shall be appointed by the Governor on the advice of the Chief Minister.
(3) Each province shall establish the following public service commissions for its respective province:
(a) Punjab Public Service Commission Ordinance, 1978
(b) Sindh Public Service Commission Ordinance, 1973
(c) The North-West Frontier Province Public Service Commission Ordinance, 1973
(d) Balochistan Public Service Commission Act, 1974
3. Officials of the Provincial Public Service Commission
The general duties of the Public Service Commission established in each province are as follows:
(a) conducting tests and examinations for initial appointment to provincial jobs and posts relating to the affairs of the province;
(b) conducting tests and examinations for recruitment to posts in any corporation, autonomous body or organization established by the Provincial Government;
(c) To advise the Government on matters relating to the terms and conditions of the members of the provincial service or persons holding posts related to the affairs of the province.
4. Annual reports
The Commission is required to submit an annual report of its performance to the Governor and the Governor is required to arrange for a copy of the report to be submitted to the Provincial Assembly.
5. Provincial Civil Servants Act
(1) In order to regulate the appointment of persons in the employment of the provinces and the terms and conditions of their employment and to make rules regarding the subsidiary matters related thereto, each Provincial Assembly shall pass the following Civil Servants Act for its province. done;
(a) The Punjab Civil Servants Act, 1974
(b) Sindh Civil Servants Act, 1973
(d) Civil Servants Act Khyber Pakhtunkhwa, 1973
(d) Balochistan Civil Servants Act, 1974
(2) In every Act necessary terms are defined. The terms and conditions of employment of civil servants have been defined.
Acts of each province governing appointments to civil posts, appointment, probationary period of persons, their promotion, promotion, posting and transfer, termination of service, retirement from service, conduct, performance and discipline, pay, leave, pension (graduation), Explains about capital sponsorship, welfare capital and group insurance and right of appeal/petition.
6. Miscellaneous Rules and Regulations for Provincial Civil Servants
(1) Each Provincial Government has enacted Acts on various subjects through its respective Assembly in relation to the employment matters of its civil servants.
(2) In exercise of the powers delegated under the Provincial Civil Servants Act, each provincial government has framed detailed rules regarding appointment and conditions of employment, promotion and transfer, qualification and discipline, conduct, leave appeal/petition etc. .
Chapter 15
Provincial Finance
1. Provincial Consolidated Fund
All revenue received by the Provincial Government, all loans issued by that Government and all sums received by it in respect of repayment of any loan shall form part of a consolidated fund to be called the Provincial Fund.
2. Official accounts
All other such sums shall be deposited in the official account of the province which;
(a) received by or on behalf of the Provincial Government; or
(b) received or submitted to the High Court or any other court established under the jurisdiction of the Province.
3. Annual Balance Sheet/Budget
The Provincial Government in respect of each financial year,
The provincial government will present the estimated income and expenditure status of this year before the provincial assembly.
The following amounts shall be shown separately in the annual balance sheet:
(a) such sums as may be required to meet the expenses which are prescribed by the Constitution to be payable to the Provincial General Fund; And
(b) such sums as may be required to meet such other expenditure as may be proposed to be paid out of the Provincial General Fund; and
(c) Distinction shall be kept between the expenses and other expenses incurred in the calculation of income.
4. Expenditure due on Provincial Consolidated Fund
(1) The following expenses shall be chargeable to the Provincial General Fund:
(a) Gratuity payable to the Governor and other expenses incidental to his office.
Advice which will be payable to:
(b) Judges of the High Court
(c) Speaker and Deputy Speaker; provincial assembly
(2) administrative expenses of the offices of the High Court and the Provincial Assembly, including the allowances payable to their officers and employees;
(3) All debt obligations, the payment of which is the responsibility of the provincial government,
including interest, expenditure on outstanding capital, repayment of capital or outstanding or other expenditure incurred in connection with the acquisition of loans and the repayment and disbursement of debt on the guarantee of the Provincial General Fund;
(4) sums required to comply with any judgment, decree or award of any court or tribunal against any province; And
(5) such other sums as may be declared as due under the Constitution or by an Act of the Provincial Assembly.
5. Procedures for the annual budget/status statement
(1) That part of the annual balance sheet which relates to the expenditure due from the Provincial Fund shall be debated in the Provincial Assembly but shall not be submitted for voting by the Provincial Assembly.
(2) Demands: the part of the annual balance sheet that is related to other expenses; The demands shall be submitted in the form of money to the Provincial Assembly and this Assembly shall be empowered to approve or disapprove any demand,
or have power to allow a demand subject to the reduction of an amount specified therein;
(3) No demand shall be made without the recommendation of the Provincial Government.
6. Validation of approved expenditure table
(1) The Chief Minister shall endorse with his signature a table specifying as follows:
(a) the specification of the sums which have been approved by the Provincial Assembly or which are contemplated to be approved;
(b) the specification of the various sums which are required to meet the expenditure due from the Provincial General Fund but no sum shall exceed the sum shown in the statement of affairs previously presented to the Assembly;
(c) The approved table shall be tabled in the Provincial Assembly but shall not be allowed to be debated or polled.
(d) No expenditure from the Provincial General Fund shall be deemed to be formally sanctioned unless it has been specified in an approved schedule and the said schedule has been laid before the Provincial Assembly in accordance with the procedure provided in the Constitution.
7. Supplementary and Excess Amounts
If it is known about a financial year that
(a) the amount authorized to be spent on a particular service during the current financial year is insufficient or there is a need to spend on a new service which is not included in the annual balance sheet for that year; or
(b) an amount has been spent on a service during a financial year in excess of the amount approved for that service for that year;
Therefore, the Provincial Government shall have the authority to approve expenditure from the Provincial General Fund, whether such expenditure is due from this fund under the Constitution or not.
Also, a supplementary balance sheet or surplus balance sheet shall be submitted before the Provincial Assembly, in which the amount of the said expenditure shall be recorded.
8. Accounts Payable
The Provincial Assembly shall have the power to approve any amount of estimated expenditure for any part of a financial year, not exceeding three months, pending the completion of the prescribed referendum procedure and the approval of the table of expenditure. Give any prior approval for Ho.
9. Power to sanction expenditure in case of dissolution of the Assembly
In case of dissolution of the Provincial Assembly, for approving the amount for the estimated expenditure,
The Provincial Government may sanction expenditure from the Provincial General Fund for any period not exceeding four months in a financial year, pending the completion of the procedure laid down in the Constitution and the approval of the expenditure table approved for the expenditure. .
Chapter 16
Accountant General of Pakistan
(Auditor General of Pakistan)
1. Appointment of Auditor General/Accountant General
According to Article 168 of the Constitution, the President appoints an Auditor General/Accountant General. Before assuming office, the Auditor General/Accountant takes oath before the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court of Pakistan (Supreme Court of Pakistan).
The text of the oath is listed in the Third Schedule of the Constitution.
2. Duties and powers of Auditor General/Accountant General with respect to provinces
(a) Calculations
(1) In addition to the responsibilities of the Federation, the Accountant shall also be responsible for keeping the accounts of the Supreme Provinces. The President may order the keeping of accounts of an autonomous body established by a province.
(2) The Governor may, if he so desires, after consultation with the Auditor General/Accountant General, by rules, provide for the removal of the Accountant General from the responsibility of preparing the accounts of a particular service or department of the province.
(3) The Auditor General/Accountant General shall prepare a statement of accounts (including closed accounts) every year from the accounts prepared by him and those of other persons responsible for keeping official accounts.
which shall record the annual receipts and disbursements for the purposes of the Province fully explained in the respective periods.
shall then submit these accounts to the Government of the Province on such date as he may fix with the consent of the Government concerned.
(4) The Auditor-General/Accountant-General shall comply with the general or special orders of the Governor-General to show any particular matter or matters of a special nature under specified periods in the accounts.
However, the Governor shall consult the Auditor General/Accountant General before issuing such orders as mentioned above.
(b) General statement of financial position
It shall be the duty of the Auditor General/Accountant General to submit a general financial status report to the President every year.
In this general financial statement he shall include a summary of the accounts of the Federation and all the provinces for the previous year and the particulars of their arrears and liabilities.
and it shall include all such information about their financial situation as the President may direct to be included in this statement.
(c) Accounting (Audit)
(1) It shall be the duty of the Auditor General/Accountant General to:
(a) to account for all expenditure incurred out of the revenue of the Provinces and to ascertain whether the sums shown in the accounts were lawfully available and for the services and purposes for which they were made; They have been used
and whether the expenditure is consistent with the authority under which the expenditure is incurred;
(b) audit/account all provincial transactions relating to loans, deposits, outstanding funds, advances, pending accounts and remittances;
(c) audit the commercial, industrial and profit and loss accounts and individual balance sheets kept under the department of the Governor of a province;
(d) audit/audit any authorized body or institution established by the province and in each case submit a report to the Governor about the audited expenditure, transactions or accounts.
(2) The Auditor-General/Accountant-General shall, with the approval of the Governor-General, or if he so directs, audit/account and submit a report of the following:
(a) in respect of any department of the Provincial Government;
(b) in respect of store accounts maintained in any office or department of the Provincial Government.
(3) The accounts of the Provinces shall be kept in such form and in accordance with such principles and methods as the Auditor General/Accountant General may prescribe with the approval of the President.
3. Reports of the Auditor General/Accountant General
According to Article 171 of the Constitution, reports of the Accountant General relating to a province are submitted to the Governor of that province who presents them to the Provincial Assembly.
Chapter 17
Elections and Caretaker Cabinet
1. Conduct of elections
(1) At the end of the five-year term of the National Assembly in terms of Article 224 of the Constitution, unless the Assembly is dissolved earlier, general elections shall be held within sixty days immediately following the day on which the term of the Assembly expires. to be
And the results of the election shall be announced within fourteen days at most from the close of polling.
(2) When the National Assembly is dissolved before the end of its term, a general election to the Assembly shall be held within ninety days from the date of dissolution and the results of the election shall be declared not later than fourteen days before the close of polling. will go
2. Supervisory Cabinet
(1) On dissolution of the National Assembly after the completion of its term or on dissolution under Article 58 or Article 112, the President shall appoint a Caretaker Cabinet.
The President will select the Caretaker Prime Minister with the advice of the Prime Minister of the National Assembly to be dismissed and the Leader of the Opposition.
(2) The members of the Provincial Caretaker Cabinet, including the Caretaker Prime Minister and his immediate family members (spouses and children) shall not be eligible to participate in the elections held immediately after the said Assembly.
(3) In the event that the Prime Minister of the outgoing National Assembly and the Leader of the Opposition do not agree on the appointment of a person as caretaker Prime Minister,
Within three days of the dissolution of that Assembly, they shall both forward two names nominated by them to a committee immediately constituted by the Speaker of the National Assembly, which shall consist of eight members of the outgoing National Assembly or Senate. .
The committee will have equal representation of the government and the opposition.
These members will be equally nominated by the Prime Minister and the Leader of the Opposition.
If the members of the opposition are less than five in any assembly, all those members shall be members of the aforesaid committee and the committee shall be deemed to be formally constituted.
(4) Within three days of the referral of the matter, a committee consisting of eight members shall finalize the name of the Caretaker Prime Minister.
If this committee fails to take a final decision within three days, the names of the nominated persons will be sent to the Election Commission of Pakistan for a final decision within two days.
(5) Until the caretaker Prime Minister is appointed, the incumbent Prime Minister shall hold office.
Chapter 18
Administrative division into provinces
1. Province
(1) In Pakistan, India and many other countries, the district functions as a local unit of government.
It symbolizes the authority of the state and the effective management of the government.
(2) For regional administration each province is divided into divisions, districts, sub-divisions and tehsils.
The head of the division is the commissioner, the head of the district is the deputy commissioner, the head of the subdivision is the assistant commissioner and the head of the tehsil is the tehsildar.
(3) There are a total of 28 divisions and 234 districts in the four provinces of Pakistan. The divisions do not include the Capital Territory of Islamabad and the Federally Administered Tribal Areas.
2. Balochistan Province (Divisions and Districts)
Administratively, Balochistan province has 6 divisions and 32 districts.
Divisions and Districts of Balochistan Province
Note: Each district is divided into tehsils. The total number of tehsils in Balochistan is 137.
3. Khyber Pakhtunkhwa Province (Divisions and Districts)
Administratively, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa province has 7 divisions and 26 districts.
Divisions and Districts of Khyber Pakhtunkhwa Province
Note: Each district is divided into Tehsils. The total number of Tehsils in Khyber Pakhtunkhwa is 0.5.
4. Punjab Province (Divisions and Districts)
Administratively, Punjab province has 9 divisions and 46 districts.
Divisions and Districts of Punjab Province
Note: Each district is divided into tehsils. The total number of tehsils in Punjab is 121.
5. Sindh Province (Divisions and Districts)
Sindh province has 6 divisions and 29 districts administratively.
Divisions and Districts of Sindh Province
Note: Each district is divided into tehsils. The total number of tehsils in Sindh is 139.
